Current Commentary: Reflections on the Import of Japanese Aged Rice 46

Japan's new grain harvest is abundant, and aged rice stocks have reached over 11 million stones this year, not including the surpluses in Korea and Taiwan. Therefore, 50,000 bags of aged rice are being dumped in our country. Each bag contains 150 pounds, and its price is only 6.3 yuan. We do not want to use excessively emotional or inflammatory language here. Considering our country as an agricultural nation, it relies solely on agricultural products to offset the import of foreign goods in terms of international balance of payments. However, in recent years, our country's handicraft products, such as porcelain and lacquerware, have been declining daily. The silk industry has also plummeted. Even if our political capabilities are comparable to those of the great powers, this kind of excessive import leakage is enough to cause extremely serious economic consequences. Moreover, in the past six months, the import of foreign rice, foreign wheat, and other miscellaneous grains has reached over 100 million. The impact on rural areas is self-evident.

Japan is a late-developing industrial nation. The agricultural population accounts for only about 60% of the total population. Its domestic agricultural food and raw materials are insufficient to meet its needs. This has always been the case. Moreover, after the global economic panic and frenzy struck, Japan was also inevitably plunged into a state of recession. However, because it is a light industrial nation and has not completely shed its agricultural production form, it has suffered less damage than other countries. In addition, the Japanese militarists have always regarded war preparation as the way to solve all problems, stimulating general production through military industry. In agriculture, they only aim for self-sufficiency. As a result, the theory of controlling rice has recently resurfaced. Overproduction of rice and market stagnation have led to an excess of stock. Because of excessive stock, rice prices cannot help but fall. The amount of the fall has even gone below the cost of production, and the hardship of rural areas is becoming even more severe. According to the current rural economic situation in Japan, the total debt of farmers has reached 7 billion yen. Each farmer is in debt for more than 1,000 yen.

Not only is rural finance exhausted and there is no way to borrow money, but some people are even filling their stomachs with miscellaneous grains, unable to get a full meal. On the other hand, although there is prosperity in the military industry in the cities, it cannot reverse the decline of the entire society. Therefore, unemployed people have nowhere to turn, and overseas immigration has become a mere fantasy. (This economic panic is global. The East experienced the panic later, but the damage is more profound. Therefore, it is not easy for overseas Chinese businesses to stabilize.) The unemployed population in large cities cannot be relocated abroad and cannot help but flow back into the countryside, making the rural areas even more unstable. This situation is reflected in the entire society. Therefore, so-called radical ideas have infiltrated the sharpening of extreme militarism. Conflicting contradictions have formed the current situation in Japan.

The Japanese warlords, at this critical juncture, are not only unwilling to give up their military policies, but are becoming increasingly tense. Strengthening land equipment, supplementing naval power, building steel plants, and controlling grain are all being planned. This sale of aged rice was originally rice stored in Japanese government warehouses for military use during wartime. Now, partly because the time has been long and they fear it will spoil, and partly because of the abundant agricultural harvest, they are taking the opportunity to replace it. Therefore, this sale of aged rice by Japan is superficially only a kind of dumping, but in reality, it contains serious military implications.

Since our China is an agricultural nation, it cannot be like the countries of the Americas supplying the world with food, but at least it should be self-sufficient, so that the people have no hunger. However, in recent decades, rural areas have gradually declined. Coastal cities such as Shanghai, Guangzhou, and Tianjin all rely on foreign rice and foreign wheat for their livelihood. Even small and medium-sized cities along the Yangtze River and the coast rely on imported food. This situation may not be a cause for concern in peacetime, but in today's uncertain world political situation, with the serious confrontation between Germany and France in Europe, the irreconcilable relationship between Germany and Italy, the intense economic competition between Britain and Japan in the Far East, the start of the naval arms race between Japan and the United States, and the increasingly deteriorating relationship between Japan and the Soviet Union, we are in a difficult position. Given the current tense situation and the weakness of our own strength, the issue of people's food is also very important to our self-defense and must be planned in advance.

Page 8

Past Work and Future Directions of the National Economic Council 47

Highways, Water Conservancy, Public Health, Sericulture, Rural Development

First Plenary Meeting to be Held Next Week

(Nanjing) The National Economic Council was formally established on October 5th and has been actively carrying out various tasks. It has also established the Cotton Industry Control Committee as a prelude to the implementation of economic control. Song Ziwen, a standing committee member of the council, has arrived in Nanjing from Shanghai. The first plenary meeting of the committee is scheduled to be held next week. A reporter from the Central News Agency, recognizing that the work of the council is urgently needed following its establishment, visited a responsible person of the council on the 20th to inquire about the council's past work and future directions. A brief summary of the information is as follows: In the autumn of the 20th year of the Republic of China, the National Government established the National Economic Council to promote economic construction and improve the people's livelihood. The council was intended to be the central hub for coordinating, designing, and implementing national economic construction plans, with the aim of promptly realizing urgent and important construction or reconstruction projects. However, given the magnitude and complexity of the matter, careful deliberation and planning were deemed necessary. Therefore, in November of the 20th year of the Republic of China, a preparatory office was first established to handle all preparatory matters related to the National Economic Council and to act as the secretariat before the full council was established. However, shortly after its establishment, the country was beset by internal and external troubles. In addition to the ravages of floods, foreign aggression followed, and the disturbances of the Communist bandits were particularly harmful, resulting in huge expenditures of national resources. Furthermore, the impact of the global economic downturn was felt, and the domestic economy repeatedly experienced panic. All of these factors undermined political stability and hindered the progress of planned work. Nevertheless, even in this difficult period, the council was able to adhere to its original purpose and strive to engage in various construction projects, laying the foundation for the permanent organization of the council. This is truly commendable. At the time of its establishment, Chiang Kai-shek, the President of the Executive Yuan, served as the Chairman of the council, and Song Ziwen, the Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, served as the Vice Chairman. Heads of relevant economic construction departments of the central government, as well as leaders from various industrial and economic sectors, served as committee members. After its establishment, the preparatory office was ordered to convene the first committee meeting. Subsequently, the directions set by this meeting were implemented separately in various projects. Based on the needs of project implementation, five specialized committees were established successively for highways, engineering, health, education, and rural development, as well as three institutions: the Highway Bureau, the Engineering Bureau, and the Central Hygiene Facilities Experimental Bureau. These committees and bureaus were able to fulfill their duties in researching, recommending, implementing, and supervising various economic construction matters, serving as an arm of the government. Furthermore, they were established separately based on established directions and have already taken initial shape. The organizational structure of the technical organs of the National Economic Council was largely completed during the preparatory period. The original organizational structure during the preparatory period is illustrated in the attached diagram. The work during the preparatory period can be summarized as follows: (1) Highways: Recognizing that the development of transportation is a prerequisite for solving all economic problems in China, the council began to supervise the construction of inter-provincial highways in May of the 21st year of the Republic of China. At the same time, it raised road construction funds and allocated loans on a regular basis to supplement the insufficient road construction funds in various provinces. The inter-provincial highways planned and supervised by the Highway Bureau of the council include two major systems: the inter-provincial highways of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces, and the inter-provincial highways of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Hunan provinces. The construction cost of the three-province highways was budgeted at a total of 3,199,000 yuan, and the construction cost of the seven-province highways was estimated at approximately 10,000,000 yuan. The three-province highway system includes six connecting highways, of which the Nanjing-Hangzhou, Shanghai-Hangzhou, Nanjing-Wuhu, Suzhou-Jiashan, and Changxing-Yixing lines have been completed and opened to traffic. Only the Hangzhou-Huizhou road is facing more difficult construction, but it is expected to be completed by the end of October this year. The seven-province highway system is over 22,000 kilometers long, of which 2,000 kilometers have been completed. As a result, over 8,000 kilometers of highways can be connected and interconnected. In addition to supervising the construction of highways in various provinces, the work of the Highway Bureau includes the construction of test roads with various types of pavements, the training of highway engineering personnel, the compilation of highway dictionaries, and the investigation and research on road construction materials, transportation, surveying, highway construction costs, and oil mines in Sichuan Province. (2) Water Conservancy Projects: China is an agricultural country, and droughts and floods are the greatest harm to the people's livelihood. The council recognized the importance of river works and water conservancy. In the past, water conservancy work was mostly focused on relief efforts, the completion of unfinished projects transferred by the Flood Relief Committee, or the establishment of engineering bureaus for implementation. It engaged in the reinforcement and heightening of the main dikes of the Yangtze, Huai, Han, and Gan rivers to prevent floods, the installation of numerous culverts along the Huai River dikes for irrigation, the dredging of the rivers in the Lixiahe area to discharge the water from the Grand Canal into the Huai River, and the construction of tidal gates at Doulonggang and Hebei River to prevent the backflow of seawater tides and to promote irrigation and navigation. In addition, it selected important locations along the Yellow, Luo, Sha, and Ying rivers in Henan Province to construct dikes, bridges, revetments, etc., to protect the farmland and residences of hundreds of thousands of residents along the river from flood disasters. During April and May of this year, the water level of the Yangtze River began to rise. The Engineering Bureau immediately began preparations for dike protection and flood prevention. By the end of June, the river water suddenly reached the highest level in the same month in recent years, and in some places, it was only one foot lower than the flood level in the 20th year of the Republic of China. The areas along the Yangtze River felt uneasy. Fortunately, the dikes built by the Flood Relief Committee last year had been maintained and repaired by the Engineering Bureau according to plan, and the flood disaster of the 20th year of the Republic of China was avoided from recurring today. (3) Hubei Dike Works and Dike Funds: The government, considering that the original competent authority for water conservancy dike works in Hubei Province was ineffective, transferred the responsibility to the council in November of the 21st year of the Republic of China. The council immediately supervised the Jianghan Engineering Bureau to complete over 100 annual maintenance projects within four months. It also established definite measures for dike inspection and flood prevention preparation to cope with emergencies. As for the Hubei Dike Works Special Fund Management Committee established by the council, its achievements were also quite remarkable. Its receipts and expenditures showed a surplus that was used for new and permanent water conservancy projects in Hubei Province. This year, a portion of it was used to implement the Jinshui Gate Construction Project, which had been designed for a long time but had not yet been started. Jinshui is a tributary of the Yangtze River. The Yangtze River water level is usually higher in summer than in winter, with a difference of about 50 feet. As a result, the tributary floods are a disaster, and the land on both sides becomes a swamp, especially Jinshui. Once this long-delayed gate construction project is completed, hundreds of thousands of acres of farmland can be protected. (4) Public Health: The organization of public health agencies was the beginning of technical cooperation between our country and the League of Nations. The former Ministry of Health had agreed on a plan with the Health Organization of the League of Nations, the most important of which was the establishment of the Central Hygiene Facilities Experimental Bureau. The bureau was established in the 18th year of the Republic of China. In the 21st year of the Republic of China, it was transferred to the National Economic Council. It engaged in the experimentation of various hygiene facilities and cooperated with various local governments to promote the establishment of all hygiene undertakings. It assisted the local governments of Hangzhou, Nanjing, and Shanghai in setting up various environmental hygiene matters. It also curbed the prevalence of cholera and other epidemics in various places in the 21st year of the Republic of China. It conducted malaria surveys and eradication plans in Nanjing and the Yangtze River area. In the 22nd year of the Republic of China, it cooperated with the Highway Bureau to establish six highway hygiene groups in various provinces, paying attention to protecting the health of workers, travelers, and the public. In addition, it established a rural hygiene facilities experimental area in Tangshan to promote the experimentation of rural hygiene work. It also used domestic materials to formulate medicines, researching their functions in preparation for recovering rights. At the same time, it cooperated with various local government groups to promote public health education, school hygiene, and maternal and child hygiene undertakings. It also set up various training courses within the bureau to train various hygiene administrative and technical personnel. As for the disaster area hygiene facilities that were jointly handled with the Flood Relief Committee in the 20th year of the Republic of China, they achieved particularly good results. (5) Sericulture: Regarding sericulture, sericulture experimental areas were set up in Hangzhou and Jurong, and the Nanjing, Xiaoshan, and Jintan sericulture experimental areas were assisted in conducting silkworm breeding experiments for the improvement of original Italian hybrid and local varieties. Guidance stations were set up in the experimental areas to guide farmers in various feeding methods. Although the silkworm breeding work encountered difficulties due to unfavorable weather and environment, the results were still satisfactory. In total, approximately 27,000 households benefited. (9) Rural Development: Rural development is an important issue at present. The council has focused on rural economic cooperatives and rural relief. Regarding rural economy, meticulous investigations have been conducted on farmland, rural population, land distribution, land rent, rural credit, and the main agricultural products, including their production, export, import, consumption, transportation, and improvement. Regarding rural cooperatives, various relevant materials have been collected for reference, and various research questions have been drafted. The opinions of specialists are being solicited. Once the solicitations are completed, planning and implementation can be carried out. As for rural relief undertakings, the council took over the rural relief affairs transferred by the Flood Relief Committee in June of this year. It is currently engaged in clearing up the original work of the committee as a reference for future planning. As for the experts from the League of Nations for technical cooperation who came to China, such as the International Education Inspection Group for education who came to China to investigate the Chinese education system. The members of the group included Mr. Pei Kelang, Ziwen, Tang Nahuaersiji, Huaerde Hengli Pinna, and Shadi. After completing the investigation, they wrote a book entitled "Improvement of Chinese Education" and drafted a preliminary plan for reforming Chinese education. Pan Lier, Gao Desi, Weijing, and others in the field of engineering came to China to study water conservancy, land reclamation, and flood prevention issues. Aojinji in the field of highways, Budeli in the field of water conservancy, and Bao Xize in the field of hygiene were stationed at the Highway Bureau, the Engineering Bureau, and the Central Hygiene Facilities Experimental Bureau, respectively, to assist in the work at any time. Mr. Telaigongni and Mr. Boli in the field of agricultural economics stayed in China for half a year to assist in the study of rural economic issues. Mali Ze in the field of sericulture was dedicated to the research of silkworm breeding and the improvement of silkworms. Shen Muwei and Yan Nake, who recently came to China, are studying central and local political systems, respectively. Looking at the above, although the work of the council is still minor in terms of the overall national economic construction, it is sufficient to prove that the council has the ability to bear the burden of promoting the economy amid layers of difficulties.

Ximeng and Other Leagues and Banners Telegraph to Nanjing Requesting Autonomy, Intending to Resist Aggression and Seek Survival, and Seeking a Way Out for a Small Number of People. The Mongolian Office Hosts the Press to Unofficially Release the Full Text of the Telegraph 48

(Nanjing) The government initially intended not to publish the Ximeng's telegraph requesting autonomy. Later, Mongolian representatives feared that misunderstandings would arise and rumors would spread, so they unofficially released it at a reception hosted by the Mongolian Office today. (Title omitted) In recent years, our country has been plagued by wars, famines, and disturbances, and the borderlands have been shrinking daily and foreign troubles have been deepening. Our Mongolia is close to Japan, and the pain is particularly acute. With vast lands and a small population, the weak nation has no power to resist and no way to defend. It is like meat on a chopping board, to be slaughtered by others. In the past ten years, Outer Mongolia has been plundered by Soviet Russia, and our Hulunbuir has fallen to Japan. Recently, Zhuozhao and other leagues have also been successively destroyed. The movement in Ximeng has shaken North China, and the situation is critical, causing concern throughout the country. Our Mongolian old and weak people are sitting and suffering slaughter, which is indeed their fate. Although the central government has the responsibility to support and relieve them, it is plagued by internal troubles and the situation is changing. The authorities do not even have time to save themselves. How can our Mongolia bear to ask the central government for assistance? Moreover, after the ravages of war, special envoys are dispatched from time to time to the remote areas to inquire, which proves that we are closely related and share weal and woe. Our Mongolia is deeply grateful for this. It is not impossible to be complacent and seek temporary peace in the face of borderland alerts. However, with the strong neighbors invading more and more urgently, there is no time to delay. Like sparrows living in a tent, the disaster of destruction is imminent. Complacency and seeking temporary peace are no longer allowed by the situation. Although the anxiety is great, there is no way to deal with it. If we do not force ourselves to make a decision, one day a strong enemy will overwhelm the border, and everywhere will be ruins. The accumulated weakness of Mongolia will inevitably be gradually swallowed up by the storm, causing deep concern to the central government. The collapse of the fence will lead to the death of Mongolia and affect our compatriots. The destruction of one part will lead to chaos and concern for the whole. The crime is deep. In times of crisis, the deer do not choose the shade. All our compatriots, putting themselves in the place of the Mongolian people, consider carefully for the Mongolians. Apart from self-determination and autonomy, what other way is there? We remember that Mr. Sun Yat-sen, with great difficulty, established the country, based on the autonomy of the people and taking the support of the weak as his mission. His teachings are followed by all generations. The central military is busy with affairs and has no time to worry about the remote areas. How dare our Mongolia not rise up and follow Mr. Sun's teachings, taking responsibility for self-determination and self-encouragement? The league leaders Zasak et al. have carefully examined the resolution of the 20th National Congress, which had the precedent of specially allowing Outer Mongolia to be autonomous. Therefore, on July 26th of this year, in Bailingmiao, Ujimqin League, a meeting of all officials of Inner Mongolia was convened. Everyone agreed to adopt a high degree of autonomy and establish an Inner Mongolia Autonomous Government to urgently seek unity and promotion to show what the central government could not do. With self-determination and autonomy in everything, it is hoped that the urgent situation can be reversed, the national border can be defended, and the people's will is pure. Everyone is asking for this. Therefore, they resolutely proceeded, and the atmosphere was invigorated. All considerations for responding to public opinion, coping with the environment, and implementing autonomy, in addition to the formal report to the central government for review by the league leaders Zasak Wang Gong and others, are hereby sent in advance to convey the truth of our Mongolia's promotion of autonomy. The true meaning of autonomy is that due to the urgency of the situation, the pressure of the environment, and the exhaustion of the way, we are determined to save ourselves and save the country and have to urgently plan for self-determination to remedy the danger. As for military affairs and diplomacy, which are related to the national system, our Mongolia is weak and powerless. In peacetime, we still rely on the central government for assistance. At the critical juncture of survival, all external measures rely even more on the central government. We also hope that the officials of the authorities will uphold Mr. Sun's principle of treating all people equally and the spirit of the world as one, understand their difficulties, pity their weakness, guide and encourage them to make up for their shortcomings, teach them what they do not know, and encourage their spirit of self-determination and autonomy, promoting their determination to strive for self-improvement, reforming their stubbornness, and renewing their governance. The upper levels will use this to assist the central government's earnest return to governance, and the lower levels will use this to comfort our Mongolia's eager desire, so that the people of the five races can help each other and coexist, forming a single entity. It is hoped that the danger can be reversed, the border can be secured, and the Mongolian people will be fortunate and the country will be fortunate. Sonam Pungbuutan, Right Banner Zasak Prince of Ujumqin, Xilingol League, Deputy League Leader Prince Demchugdongrub and dozens of others co-signed. (Special dispatch on the 20th)

(Nanjing) Wu Heling, Director of the Mongolian Association Office, hosted a press conference and reported that the central government has dispatched Minister Huang and Deputy Commissioner Zhao to inspect the various leagues and banners of Inner Mongolia in response to Mongolia's request for autonomy. They will surely have a clear observation and appropriate disposal. Originally, the Mongolian autonomy issue was raised during the completion of the Northern Expedition in the 17th year of the Republic of China. When the policy of supporting the self-determination and autonomy of small ethnic groups was promoted to Mongolia, the various leagues and banners had a request to establish an Inner Mongolia local government, wanting to implement autonomy within the scope of not hindering national unity. Now, Mongolian land has lost most of it due to the national government's inability to manage it. And the only remaining Xilingol and Ujimqin leagues and banners have also become fish in a cauldron. They feel that without autonomous organization, it is not enough to resist aggression and seek survival, so they have once again put forward the request for autonomy to the central government. As for their requested high degree of autonomy, it does not mean breaking away from China's independence. Some people have put the crimes of surrendering to Japan and attaching to rebellion with a background, etc. on the heads of the Mongolians. This is a statement that departs from the facts. Mongolia will never cooperate with Japan because the Mongolians are unwilling to change the league and banner system. The Japanese have already abolished the three leagues of Ulaanchab, Chahar, and Jerim, changing them into four provinces in the southeast, northwest, and they have also changed the Danzasak into a banner chief, trying to break up the unity of the league and banner chiefs everywhere. For example, they only changed the seven banners of the Josutu League and the seven banners of the southern part of the Jerim League into their respective autonomy, not allowing them to establish a common agency. Why are they abandoning this and choosing that? Therefore, we very much hope that the government should prevent the Japanese from snatching away the existing Mongolia again and not worry that Mongolia is betraying the central government. People say that this Mongolian request for autonomy is a political way out for a small number of people. As long as more positions are given, it can be resolved. In fact, the Mongolian intention in requesting autonomy is to gather all their strength to resist aggression and seek survival. The telegraph of intent has already made it very clear, and the people who signed the telegraph of intent all have their hereditary positions. Now, if their problem of resisting aggression and seeking survival is not solved, and the method of appeasing and disrupting elements is used to deal with it, it is like climbing a tree to catch fish. I hope that the government will appreciate the difficulties of Mongolia's request for autonomy and try to make it generate the power to resist foreign aggression, which will be beneficial to both the country and the local area. After the telegraph of intent was issued, it was originally scheduled to convene a meeting in Bailingmiao on September 28 to discuss the implementation methods. Later, I heard that the central government decided to send senior officials to promote it, so it has been postponed until now. In the middle, there have only been two meetings. One was on the 9th of this month. As a result, 24 people were elected to draft the organization law of the autonomous government, preparing to contact the senior officials. The other was on the 15th of this month to pass the autonomous plan. The contents are not detailed, but Yun, the league leader of the Ujimqin League, the landlord of Bailingmiao, has repeatedly telegraphed to Nanjing, expressing that he wants to seek autonomy under the support of the party and the country. During the progress of this meeting, the Japanese also convened a Mongolian banner meeting in Dolon Nor. The notices they gave to the various leagues and banners were very serious with coercion and inducement. Their intention was to prevent the Bailingmiao meeting from being held. However, the officials and representatives of the various leagues and banners still gathered in Bailingmiao as agreed, so that no one attended the Dolon Nor meeting. Now, the officials and representatives who have arrived in Bailingmiao are all eager to get a satisfactory result, so Yun, the league leader of the Ujimqin League, and Prince De, the deputy league leader of the Xilingol League (i.e., Prince De), etc., have repeatedly telegraphed to welcome the senior officials to go, and have repeatedly telegraphed to invite Heling to go. It is my duty to depart to the north in a day or two. I have three creeds for Mongolia: one is cooperation between the local and central governments, two is cooperation between the leagues and banners and the provinces and counties, and three is cooperation between the princes and commoners. This time, I will go to Bailingmiao to fulfill the autonomy of Inner Mongolia in accordance with this creed. (Special dispatch on the 20th)

(Beiping) Bailingmiao News: Prince De convened a meeting on the 9th. Due to insufficient numbers, it was changed to a preparatory meeting. 106 princes and dukes arrived and elected 23 people to draft the organization law of the autonomous government. It was passed by the general assembly on the 15th. Except for military affairs and diplomacy, which are still under the central government, the administrative affairs of Inner Mongolia are all handled by the autonomous government. The highest authority is the autonomous government. The committee has two offices under it: the Senate and the Administrative Office, as well as the Legal Committee. The Administrative Office has eight offices under it: General Affairs, Secretary, Education, Police, Industry, Transportation, Public Relations, and Construction. The autonomous government will choose one of the three places: Bailingmiao, Siziwang Banner, and Prince De's mansion, to be established. We hope for assistance from the central government. (Special dispatch on the 20th)

Wei Dexin, Counselor of the Jin-Sui Headquarters, Assassinated. Assassin Li Shu Surrenders, Claiming Revenge for His Father 53

(Taiyuan) Wei Dexin, who once served as the commander of the Jin Army regiment, the garrison commander of Jintong, and is now a counselor of the Sui Headquarters, was the city defense commander of Shuoxian during the war in Yanbei. Li is the brother of Li Shangren, the current member of the Jin Provincial Government. Later, after Yan clarified the matter, Wei was sentenced to twelve years in prison. Last year, he asked someone to mediate with Li's side and was released from prison. Li Shu, the son of Zhiren, who is over twenty years old and a graduate of an industrial college, followed Wei to the Shifangyuan Temple outside the North Gate this morning to listen to Buddha lectures. When he returned to the city, he shot Wei with a pistol on North Gate Street at about 12 o'clock and surrendered to the police station, claiming revenge for his father. The court examined the body in the evening and Wei's wife took the body away. The assassin is currently detained in the Public Security Bureau pending legal resolution. (Special dispatch on the 20th)

Jiang Que Aircraft Resists, Today Flies to Yong, Wen, then to Fujian 57

(Hangzhou) Chen Wenlin, accompanied by Wang Shenghai, the chief technician of the Naval Aviation Department, piloted the Jiang Que aircraft from the Hongqiao Airport in Shanghai at 11:40 AM on the 20th and arrived at the Qiaotou Aviation School Airport at 1:07 PM. Those welcoming them at the airfield included Fang Qingru, a member of the provincial party headquarters, Jiang Jianren, the director of the political training department of the aviation school, Zeng Jianying, Liu Xiangnv, Ye Longquan, and over a dozen representatives from the provincial government's aviation bureau, the Hangzhou city government, and various agencies, as well as Cai Zhuping and other instructors from the aviation school, totaling over fifty people. Chen and Wang disembarked, exchanged pleasantries with the welcomers, and posed for a group photo. Speaking to a reporter from the Central News Agency, they stated that after taking off today, the journey had been smooth. They would stay overnight in Hangzhou and leave for Fuzhou via Yong and Wen at 8:00 AM on the 21st. When passing over Yong and Wen, they would land to refuel. On the 22nd, they would fly to Xiamen and, after a two-week stop, continue flying to Guangdong and Guangxi to complete the nationwide land flight. They would then switch to a seaplane and take off from Xiamen to conduct a nationwide coastline flight. The purpose is to awaken the people's universal attention and self-manufacture airplanes to engage in a practical aviation national salvation movement. (20th Central News Agency Telegraph)

Pittman Advocates Minting Silver Coins 60

Stop After Silver Price Rises To Satisfactory Value

(Washington) US Senator Pittman announced today that he is currently drafting a bill to be submitted immediately after Congress convenes, stipulating that the government freely mint silver coins, and stop minting after silver reaches a satisfactory price. He also said that free minting of silver coins can provide the minimum amount of inflationary currency, and is the only safe way to avoid the danger of inflationary banknotes. In addition, Pittman also stated that although he advocates inflationary currency arising from the minting of silver coins, he does not agree with senators who advocate issuing greenback notes to raise prices.

(19th National Telegram)

Storm Blows Japanese Ship Sinking, More Than a Hundred Passengers Missing 64

Osaka, the Kansai region of Japan has experienced storms since yesterday. At 1:20 PM today, the Yashima Maru was blown over into the sea by a strong wind off the coast of Suma. The ship is a 946-ton passenger ship with 40 crew members, including Captain Shioami, and more than 100 passengers on board. By 5:00 PM, some passengers had swum to the shore or been rescued by neighboring ships. By 6:00 PM, 43 people had been rescued, and the whereabouts of others were still unknown. Most of them had died tragically. Among the passengers were two foreigners and the Ehime Prefectural Interior Minister. The ship lost its rudder and tilted, sinking into the sea in less than ten minutes, so there was no time to escape. The Kobe Maritime Police Station and the shipping company have telegraphed three ships, including the Hong Kong Maru, which are sailing nearby, to rescue them, but they are unable to do anything in the face of the raging waves. (20th China United Telegram)

(Zhenjiang) The provincial government resolved on the 20th: (1) To approve the measures to organize the financial administration of the province, in three points: 1. To unify the financial administration, all financial matters shall be directly managed by the Finance Department. Except for education funds, which are independent, all income and expenditure funds of various agencies in the province shall be deposited in the treasury. 2. To stipulate the measures for the receipt and expenditure of special funds, the expenditure of special funds for various constructions shall be reported to the Finance Department on a ten-day basis, and the expenditure must be signed and issued by the Finance Department in conjunction with the competent authority. 3. To implement the treasury system throughout the province, the income of each county shall be deposited in the Jiangsu Branch of the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Agricultural Bank, and Fourth Bank, and shall not be arbitrarily delayed. Fang Ji's Troops Are Being Disbanded, After Inspection, There Are a Total of More Than 6,000 Officers and Soldiers, Transported in Batches to Baoding for Reorganization and Separation. Fang Zhenwu and Sun Heqiao Escape Danger, Ji Hongchang Has Secretly Arrived in Tianjin 83

Beiping Communication: After Fang Zhenwu and Ji Hongchang left the army, their troops, led by Mi Wenhe, were mobilized to the areas of Dongxiduling Village, Tian Ge Village, Dongjia Village, and Qianhou Heyu to await inspection. The Military Branch sent Huang Shiyue to inspect the troops on the morning of the 17th in conjunction with Lu Ji, the Chief of Staff of the 32nd Army. By the afternoon of yesterday (18th), it was completely completed. Fang Ji's troops originally had more than 14,000 people. The inspection revealed that only more than 6,000 remained, including 194 officers, 116 soldiers, and 86 students from Fang Zhenwu's headquarters, about 3,000 officers and soldiers from Zhao Chengkai's troops of Fang's department, 390 officers and 82 soldiers from Mi Wenhe's department, about 200 cavalrymen and 100 horses from Wang Ying's department, and 1,029 officers and 951 soldiers from Ji Hongchang's department, totaling 6,558 people. The number of guns, more than 1,600 from Fang's department, about 470 from Ji's department, totaling about 2,000 guns. After the inspection was completed, Huang Shiyue returned to Ping last night (18th) to report. Fang Ji's troops were ordered to concentrate in the Sunhe area and transport them to Baoding in batches for reorganization. The first two batches departed from Sunhe South at 5:00 AM this morning (19th), passed Taipingzhuang at 8:00 AM, and arrived in Qinghe in the afternoon. From Qinghe, they took a car to Fengtai and headed to Baoding. The remaining troops are also being transported in succession. Once all the troops are transported to Baoding, they will begin reorganization and separation. Because Fang Ji's troops have surrendered their arms and been transported away from the war zone, the armies in the front have begun to demobilize separately from today. The Japanese army in the Niulanshan Huairou area is also gradually withdrawing towards Miyun Gubeikou.

Fang Ji's whereabouts are unknown, which has caused suspicion from the outside world. According to reliable sources, when Fang Ji personally met with Shang Zhen, Xu Tingyao, and Guan Linzheng at Fengjiaying on the 16th, they agreed on all the measures. Fang Ji decided to leave the army and go to Tianjin to go abroad. A certain general who was present, using the excuse of changing clothes, notified a certain regiment stationed in Sunhe by telephone in another room, ordering them to send troops to detain Fang Zhenwu when he crossed the defense line, and wait for instructions. Ji could be released. The certain general's move was carried out under orders. When a certain general went out, some people in the seat suspected him. Later, Fang Ji left Fengjiaying in a car at 4:00 PM. Shang Zhen, because he had become sworn brothers with Fang Zhenwu and had a very deep friendship, gave Fang 5,000 yuan in paper money as travel expenses. At that time, Fang was still wearing a Zhongshan suit, and Shang also instructed him to change his clothes to make it more convenient on the way. Seeing Shang's sincerity and gratitude, Fang burst into tears, and hearing the words of changing clothes, he could not help but change his complexion in a miserable way, and immediately changed his clothes, with the feeling of a hero's end. When boarding the car, Shang and Fang Ji reluctantly bid farewell, urging them to take care. Xu Tingyao also stepped forward to shake hands with Fang and said goodbye. Fengjiaying is the defense zone of Shang's department. Eight or nine miles to the south is Sunhe, which is the defense zone of a certain army and is garrisoned by a certain army. Fang took five guards and took another car. Ji took the same car as Liu Diquan, a representative of the Beijing charity organization. Seven or eight miles away from Fengjiaying, when they arrived at Sunhe Bridge, a regiment of a certain army rushed up and blocked the way. The soldiers all held guns in a aiming posture, and the situation was very serious. After the car stopped, the soldiers shouted, "Is Fang Zhenwu in the car? Chairman Huang is setting up a banquet tonight at the Water Company (Sunhe has a water plant, about a mile away from Sunhe Bridge. The tap water in Beiping is supplied from there) to wash away the dust. Fang and Ji heard the words in silence. Then Liu Diquan replied that Fang Ji's car was still behind and would arrive soon. The army believed it to be true, withdrew some troops, and waited separately, but forced it to drive to the door of the water company and wait for inspection. Seeing that the situation was not good, Fang excused himself to get off the bus and escaped on the way. Ji arrived at the door of the water company, and after inspection, was allowed to leave. After Fang Ji left, a certain general rushed from Fengjiaying to Sunhe to inquire about Fang's whereabouts, but it was as if he had disappeared. He immediately sent people to search in all directions, but there was no trace of him. Ji Hongchang and Liu Diquan and others left Sunhe and traveled more than ten miles. The car broke down and abandoned the car to walk, and stayed overnight in a wild village, arrived in Ping before dawn, and rested briefly. That night, they took a bus to Tianjin, first staying in a hotel, and moved to a certain concession yesterday morning. It is heard that he has left Tianjin today and gone elsewhere, and the direction is unknown. Fang Zhenwu escaped from Sunhe and has not been found. According to a certain source, Fang traveled by night and slept by day, passing through Sanhe Wuqing, and arrived in Tianjin last night. Whether this is reliable remains to be proven. (October 19)

Henan Province Establishes Emergency Relief and Investigation Office, Engineering Office Also Established 84
