Fan County Reports Another Surge in Water, The Number of Victims Has Also Increased for Several Days, The Department of Construction Plans to Dredge the Zhao Wang River 85

Jinan Communication, According to the report of the medical team of the Yellow River Water Disaster Relief Committee's Sanitation Group, south of the Jin Dyke in Fan County, the floodwaters are flowing horizontally, and the villages are still in the waves. The residents on both sides are using ferries to cross. There are more than 19,000 victims who have no homes to return to, more than 22,700 people who are currently starving, and 21,700 poor people who will be hungry in the future. For several days, the number of victims has also increased by more than 300 households every day. In the past, each person could get four bowls of porridge per meal, but now they only get one or two bowls. The number of patients is 938 on the 9th, 257 on the 10th, 236 on the 11th, 264 on the 12th, 224 on the 13th, and 293 on the 14th. The number of patients in the Jining disaster area is 566, 53 on the 6th, 84 on the 7th, 199 on the 10th, and 178 on the 11th. According to a telegram from the Fan County magistrate, the water between the Jin Dyke and the Great Dyke has increased by 8 centimeters due to the fact that the breach in Shitou Village has not yet been repaired, and strict prevention is already underway.

The Zhao Wang River, Wanfu River, and Zhu Shui River are the three major rivers in western Shandong. The Department of Construction has organized the water flow in western Shandong in recent years, and the Wanfu and Zhu Shui rivers have been dredged. Only the Zhao Wang River has not been completed. This year, the Yellow River breached in Hebei and Henan, and the flood flowed eastward, and western Shandong suffered a severe water disaster. The Wanfu and Zhu Shui rivers have drainage efficiency, and the counties along the rivers suffered less. The counties along the Zhao Wang River suffered severely. Now that the water has receded, and after the pain has subsided, the Zhao Wang River should be actively dredged. The Department of Construction has now completed the planning and estimation. It is estimated that the earthwork requires 881,500 yuan, and the box masonry embankment requires 180,000 yuan, for a total of 1,061,500 yuan. It will be requested from the provincial government, and the funds will be started. Since the water disaster occurred in western Shandong, all sectors have worked hard to donate in order to gather strength and provide relief. For example, civil servants donate their salaries to help relief, and actors contribute their talents to help relief. Recently, the military clothing shops in Ji City are also very concerned about the disaster victims. The managers of Xinghua Xinjun Clothing Shop, Wang Dingzhen, Tongli Gongjun Clothing Shop, Wang Chichen, Yihe Yongjun Clothing Shop, Xu Zhongsan, Yonghu Maojun Clothing Shop, Jiang Shaoqing, Huasheng Jun Clothing Shop, Sui Yinpu, Dingsheng Jun Clothing Shop, Li Yinkai, and Dingyu Jun Clothing Shop, Zhang Yisan, and other seven military clothing shops jointly donated 200 sets of cotton clothes to help the disaster victims in western Shandong. The cotton clothes have been transported to the provincial relief committee and will be transported to the disaster area for distribution soon. (October 19)

Zhang Qun Cables Chiang Kai-shek with Suggestions for Reforming the Political System; Chiang Disapproves Changes to the Current System of Commissioners, but Approves Subsidies for Impoverished Counties in Hubei 86

Hankou Correspondence: Provincial Chairman Zhang Qun, having previously received from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek a mandate to revitalize county administration, was ordered to draft concrete implementation measures and telegraph them for approval. The telegraph included three proposed measures: (1) Joint offices for various departments; (2) Reforming the administrative commissioner system; (3) Temporary subsidies for county administration expenses. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek replied, stating that, except for the first item, which had been telegraphed to the chairmen of the seven provinces of Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Anhui, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, and Jiangsu to solicit their opinions, the second item was deemed unnecessary for discussion and the third item could be implemented as proposed. The exchange of telegrams between Chiang and Zhang was released by the provincial government on the 18th, and is disclosed as follows:

Zhang Qun's telegram to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek reads: "One, Respectfully to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in Nanchang, respectfully acknowledging receipt of your instructions. That local officials should be close to the people has been emphasized in all dynasties, with great importance placed on their selection. In recent years, official corruption has worsened daily, and the position of county magistrate has become increasingly trivial. Laws and regulations are increasingly stringent, but governance is increasingly derelict, causing hardship for both officials and the people, a situation that could not be worse. Your Excellency deeply considers governance to be rooted in channeling human and material resources to the counties. We, your subordinates, follow the current and propagate your intentions, daring not to deviate from your virtuous aims in implementing them. However, the province's budget, as determined by Your Excellency, has already seen rigorous cuts to all superfluous organizations and redundant personnel last year. Now, after further review by the various departments, there are truly no organizations that can be cut, nor any redundant personnel that can be eliminated. The expenses for the personnel of this government are reported monthly, and we trust they have been carefully scrutinized. Moreover, the total annual expenses for the seventy counties in this province are a little over eight hundred eighty thousand yuan. Increasing this by one-third would require over five hundred eighty thousand yuan annually, and even increasing it by half would require over four hundred forty thousand yuan. This cannot be compensated by merely cutting a few redundant personnel. We believe that organizational expenses are determined by the current organizational structure. If, within the current structure, the tedium of layered submissions and transfers could be eliminated, the effect of reducing personnel and streamlining administration would be naturally achieved. County administration is an integral part of provincial administration; if provincial administration is not thoroughly rectified, it will be difficult to achieve the goal of revitalizing county administration. Your Excellency already listed the shortcomings of the current committee system of the provincial government during the first internal affairs conference, and proposals for a provincial governor system were also made at the Third Plenary Session. However, the matter is of great importance and cannot be completed overnight. For the sake of facilitating implementation, the various departments of the provincial government could, under the current system, first consolidate their offices and conduct official business jointly. All official documents would be issued in the name of the provincial government, and the heads of each department would countersign matters under their jurisdiction. This would eliminate the need for each department head to forward documents upward to the relevant ministries and the provincial government, and downward to the various counties, as well as the layered transfer of documents between departments. Following this model, personnel expenses could naturally be reduced by half. Among the provincial government's subordinate units, apart from the expenses of the Security Bureau, which are based on the military organization system and should be discussed separately, the total expenses of the provincial government and the Western Hubei Administrative Office amount to over one million one hundred nineteen thousand yuan. If half of this amount could be saved, it would be roughly equivalent to one-fifth of the necessary county administration expenses, and the difference would not be far off. If this system is implemented, the provincial government will have unified will from above, and the counties will be free from the suffering of conflicting and complicated government orders from below. Barriers will be removed, and communication will be easier. Moreover, it will not only save expenses. This concerns the organization of the provincial government. Under the current system, the administrative inspector-general concurrently serves as the magistrate of the county in which they are stationed. The initial intention of this law was to rectify the long-standing problems in county administration by leveraging the power of the inspector-general. However, the position of the inspector-general is equal to that of the department heads, making supervision and accountability difficult when evaluating performance. Moreover, everyone has their limitations. Those skilled in political affairs may not necessarily be knowledgeable in military matters, and those diligent in serving the people may be negligent in observing officials. The inspector-general, in their own person, concurrently serves as the security commander and the county magistrate. Not only is it difficult to combine these talents, but their energy is also likely to be insufficient. Although there are deputy commanders and secretaries assisting them, if they do not personally oversee matters, problems are bound to arise. If the expenses of each county are increased, and the financial resources are sufficient, governance will naturally be easier. It seems unnecessary for the inspector-general to concurrently hold these positions. Instead, capable and virtuous individuals should be carefully selected to focus on their responsibilities, so that all can advance equally without undue emphasis on one aspect. As for the system of inspector-generals, it seems that it can also be changed to some extent, with the position of security commander as their primary role, while also overseeing inspections. The division of each district should also be based primarily on bandit suppression and military affairs, consolidating them into four or five districts, so that the population is roughly equal, without being too small or too large, in order to trial the division of military districts and establish a foundation for conscription. This concerns the organization of administrative inspector-generals. The above suggestions involve changing the current system. We humbly await your selection and implementation of any merits. However, county administration expenses urgently need to be increased and should not be delayed. Since this year's budget has already been determined, it is proposed that, excluding the counties concurrently administered by the inspector-generals, a total of fifty-nine counties be subsidized at a rate of three hundred yuan per month, regardless of the county's classification, starting from the second half of this year. This will require an additional expense of one hundred six thousand two hundred yuan for six months, which will be initially allocated from the provincial treasury and then offset later. This is a temporary subsidy measure for this year. This is the extent of our financial capabilities in this province. If the financial situation improves slightly next year, or if the current system is changed, new regulations will be formulated. As for the allocation of county administration expenses, the treatment of county magistrates and their staff, and the terms of office and performance evaluations, all relevant matters will be thoroughly discussed by the department and submitted for approval. We dare to exert our foolishness to answer your insightful questions. We respectfully request your instructions. Zhang Qun bows."

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's reply to Zhang Qun briefly stated: (The proposed methods for reforming the current system of provincial government and commissioners are not without merit. The following is a separate review: (1) Already seen in the previous report, omitted for brevity.) (2) The concurrent position of commissioner and local county magistrate is the sole basis for the establishment of the commissioner system. If only undertaking inspection and not simultaneously in charge of governance, this would resemble a redundant position and would not match reality, similar to an ineffective administrator. The successful promotion of all policies must be driven by the commissioner taking up the role of county magistrate, setting an example for others. Only those who can set such an example can truly grasp the difficulties therein, and thus supervise others with clarity and effectiveness. Over the past year, ministerial orders where some progress has been made have generally been in counties managed by the commissioner, thus clearly proving the benefit. To claim that the commissioner has too many duties, bringing together literary and military affairs, observing officials, managing the public, is insufficient in terms of skill and energy, ignoring that such powers and responsibilities are generally required of a local official. The county magistrate historically has also been a leader of the defense corps or security force, with the county also under his jurisdiction for the assessment of subordinate officials. Why should this be different for the commissioner? Moreover, the organization of the commissioner's office provides for a secretary, deputy security commander, staff, and adjutants to assist him. When on patrol, the secretary or deputy commander may be sent as a substitute. This measure was provided at the beginning of the establishment. If one has concerns that the commissioner, with the full organization, has insufficient energy, what is to be said of the county magistrate who has few staff to aid them? Within a province, finding a few or even a dozen such commissioners is considered a challenge; what, then, can be said of the task of employing hundreds of county magistrates? Therefore, since it is difficult to find widely available county magistrates, if counties under the care of a commissioner are to be removed and the entire province brought into parallel progress, it would, in name, be to prevent disparity. In reality, no county would have an effective county magistrate. As the county magistrate's station would be unable to be raised, the commissioner's compensation would then have to be brought into line, somewhat reduced, although equivalent to the station of department head. Even the punishment and rewards will then be decided by the provincial council, not dissimilar to the promotion and demotion of county magistrates. In the evaluation of performance, there will be no issue of difficult oversight. What has been described here indicates that the purpose of the commissioner's establishment has not been clearly understood. Last August, the headquarters distributed instructions on the purpose of the commissioner, which may be referenced. The suggestion that commissioners should not be in charge of county magistrate is therefore to be ruled out. (3) A temporary subsidy of 300 yuan for all counties shall be provided. Once the reform of the provincial system is confirmed, remaining expenditures may be transferred to the counties. This may be put into effect. (18th day)

Qingdao's Import Trade Declines 87

The Prosperity Promotion Association Suggests that the Municipal Government Request the Organization of a Customs Duty Reduction Committee

Qingdao Correspondence: The Qingdao Prosperity Promotion Association, since its establishment, has been actively pursuing plans to promote the city's prosperity. Projects such as the purchase of model automobiles and the construction of medium-sized residences are closely related to the people's livelihood. Recently, in order to protect maritime transport from being affected by land transport, it specifically petitioned the municipal government, detailing that the development of import and export goods is closely related to the prosperity of Qingdao. It requested that the municipal government send letters to relevant parties such as the Qingdao Customs, the Jiaoji Railway Bureau, and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, requesting the prompt organization of a Customs Duty Reduction Committee to jointly discuss solutions. The original text is as follows: "We believe that there are many ways to promote the prosperity of Qingdao. Attracting tourists is certainly one method, but the fundamental lifeline lies in the development of import and export goods. The rise and fall of Qingdao is directly proportional to the development of import and export goods. Since the development of import and export goods is closely related to the prosperity of Qingdao, we observe that the current trend is that import and export goods are in danger of declining. The reason for this is the issue of customs duties. The volume of import and export goods handled by any seaport is always determined by the cost required for the goods themselves. If the cost is low, merchants will flock to it and the volume will be high. If the cost is high, merchants will bypass it and the volume will be low. The relationship between profit and loss is clearly and unmistakably shown. Most of Shandong's major export goods are transported to Shanghai and then transshipped abroad. However, the goods from Shandong to Shanghai, in addition to being transported by the Jiaoji Railway to this city and then shipped to Shanghai by sea, are also transported by land via the Tianjin-Pukou Railway and the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway. Let us compare the transportation costs of Shandong's major export goods between Jinan and Shanghai by sea and land (attached table omitted). From the table, it can be seen that the transportation costs of major goods such as crude oil, raw rice, cotton, tobacco leaves, silk cocoons, and jujubes from Jinan to Shanghai via the Tianjin-Pukou Railway are lower than the transportation costs from Jinan to Shanghai via Qingdao by sea. Merchants will always choose the route with lower costs. In the future, the trend of Shandong's major goods being transported to Shanghai will be to abandon the sea route and take the land route. If this continues, Qingdao will not only have no hope of prosperity, but will also decline day by day. The key reason why the cost of transporting Shandong's major export goods to Shanghai is lower by land than by sea is that there are no customs duties on land transport, but there are customs duties on sea transport. Although there is the Jinling Customs on land, the railway is considered inland and no customs duties are levied. We have little research on the customs duty system, but since both routes are within the country and the goods have the same destination, why is there a difference? For the sake of promoting the prosperity of Qingdao, we must promptly devise a rescue plan. The customs duty system has been in place for a long time. The Qingdao Customs has taxes, while the Jinling Customs does not. This is not a recent phenomenon. Even if we check the cargo transportation statistics of the Jiaoji Railway over the years, although there are increases and decreases, it had recovered to the original state of the twelfth year in the twentieth year (attached table omitted). Based on this example, it seems that customs duties are not affected in any way. How can we know that the situation in the country is different after the twentieth year, and that the cost of transportation is also greatly different from the twentieth year? Let us describe this as follows: Before January of the twentieth year, there were numerous internal taxes and levies in the country, and the burden of taxes on land transport between Jinan and Shanghai via Shandong, Anhui, and Jiangsu provinces can be imagined. If transported by sea, there is only Shandong province, and the taxes are simple. Even with the addition of customs duties, it is still not as heavy as the land route. This is why the volume of goods entering and leaving Qingdao port can still be maintained year by year. Since January 1, in the twentieth year, with the implementation of the 'abolition of internal taxes,' all internal taxes were swept away, and the actual cost of goods borne by land was lower than that by sea. How can the volume of import and export goods in Qingdao port not be affected by this? This is the first reason. Before the railway cargo transportation was responsible, there were many miscellaneous fees for land transportation between Jinan and Shanghai, such as escort fees, which cost several tens of yuan per car. The cost of crossing the river at Pukou was as high as one yuan and thirty yuan per ton. After the implementation of cargo liability on the Tianjin-Pukou and Shanghai-Nanjing Railways in September of last year, the escort fees were cancelled, and the cost of crossing the river at Pukou was also regulated separately due to the joint operation of Tianjin-Pukou and Shanghai-Nanjing. The current calculation is only about three yuan. In the future, when the ferry is implemented (October 10), the cost is only regulated at two yuan and five jiao. The cost of land transportation between Jinan and Shanghai has been greatly reduced due to the implementation of cargo liability and the opening of the Pukou ferry, while the cost of sea transportation remains the same. Generally, merchants will inevitably abandon this and take that. This is the second reason. In addition, it is found that the national cargo intermodal transportation has been implemented from November 1 of this year. According to the intermodal price, a reduction of one percent is given for every hundred kilometers over five hundred kilometers. The land route from Jinan to Shanghai is 1,020 kilometers, so a reduction of six percent should be given. If the goods are transferred from Qingzhou to Jinan to Shanghai, a reduction of seven percent is given. If transferred from Weixian to Jinan to Shanghai, a reduction of eight percent is given. With the reduction in the price of intermodal transportation, all goods west of Weixian will be absorbed by the land route. This is the third reason. In view of the three situations mentioned above, Qingdao port will not only be unable to absorb the goods on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway in Shandong in the future, but the goods exported from this port, that is, the goods along the Jiaoji Railway, which have always been exported through Qingdao as the only port, may also be absorbed. Isn't this the greatest fatal blow to Qingdao port? If we want to rescue it, we must find a way to make the Qingdao Customs the same as the Jinling Customs. All goods exported from this port to Shanghai will not be taxed temporarily, and will be taxed again when they are exported from Shanghai. This is the best policy. Even if this cannot be achieved, if taxes are paid at the Qingdao Customs to Shanghai, all those who do not transport exports should be regarded as inland and the customs duties should be refunded by the customs. In practice, it can still be the same as the Jinling Customs. If this is the case, land and sea transportation will be equal, and the volume of import and export goods in this port can be maintained at the previous level, and this city can achieve the goal of prosperity. We hereby submit this document to the municipal government, requesting that it send letters to the Qingdao Customs, the Jiaoji Railway Bureau, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the Chamber of Commerce, and the Native Products Association, respectively designating responsible personnel, together with representatives of the municipal government, to form a committee to jointly study and remedy the situation. This is for the public benefit. (October 19)"

Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department Announces Construction Plan: The Situation in Northern Jiangsu is More Important Than in Southern Jiangsu 88

The Director of the Jiangsu Construction Department issued a statement yesterday, recorded as follows: "(The construction of this province is complex, and the situation in northern Jiangsu is more important than in southern Jiangsu. The following are the matters that urgently need to be handled: (1) Dredging the Liu Tang River; (2) Assisting in guiding the Huai River; (3) Reclaiming the Huainan area; (4) Improving cotton cultivation; (5) Building major highways. The Liu Tang River and the Huai River are both major water conservancy projects in northern Jiangsu. In addition to the Huai River, which already has a competent authority, this department will assist in the dredging of the Liu Tang River. This department has already dispatched technician Chen Zhiding to the area yesterday to meet with the director of the Huaipi section of the public works office to conduct a survey and come up with concrete measures for soliciting labor and dredging. The Huainan area is vast, and once reclaimed, it will all become fertile land. Cotton cultivation is a specialty of northern Jiangsu, and if improved, production can be greatly increased. Highways are needed for transportation and are also very important. The matters that urgently need to be handled in southern Jiangsu are: (1) Seawall project; (2) Building sluices along the Yangtze River in the Taihu Lake basin; (3) Improving sericulture. The seawall project is very large, and the annual maintenance funds have not yet been allocated. If we want to build and repair it, it will cost several million. This matter should be discussed further, or we should ask the provincial government to designate special funds to be handled in stages. The Taihu Lake is related to the rise and fall of water conservancy in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. The most important plan is to build sluices along the Yangtze River. Sericulture is also a major part of the production in southern Jiangsu, but in recent years, it has become increasingly decadent due to its simplicity and crudeness. Unless it is thoroughly improved, it will not be enough to increase production. As for my principles of doing things, (1) be open and honest; (2) be responsible; (3) focus on production. (October 20)"

Songjiang: Demands Tax Collection Rewards to Exclude Surtaxes 89

Li Zuhua, director of the county's public funds and public property management office, said that the provincial finance department's dispatch of personnel to collect old taxes and offer rewards for success, while simultaneously applying the same reward system to the surtaxed local special levies on land, would affect the implementation of local affairs. He sent telegrams to the Executive Yuan, Ministry of Finance, Provincial Government, Provincial Finance Department, Fourth District Administrative Inspector, and other institutions, stating that the regular and surtaxes have long been divided, and the surtax is originally for local affairs. Such collection fees and late payment penalties have never been applied to the surtax. Such tax collection rewards should also be excluded in order to protect local finances and maintain the implementation of local affairs. He telegraphed a request to exempt the surtax on land from any reward system. The county executive committee also approved the Baoshan County Party's telegram to convene party departments of various counties to send representatives to the province to jointly petition the government. The county has appointed executive committee member Tan Bao as the responsible party.

Tianma Mountain Theatrical Performance Dispute 90

Zhou Jun, Lu Shixin, and Qian Jinghao, trainers of the 8th District Defense Corps, due to insufficient funding, organized a theatrical performance to raise funds, scheduled to run from the 12th to the 18th at Tianma Mountain. District Chief Zhang Tianmin, believing that theatrical performances were prohibited by the county magistrate, advised them to stop. The trainers continued to prepare, and the tickets were still issued in the name of the district corps headquarters. District Chief Zhang reported the situation, and County Magistrate Jin sent several police officers to the village to ban the performance. It was stopped after the first day. The district chief and trainers were summoned for interrogation. Zhou Jun refused to appear. Trainers Lu and Qian both blamed their actions on Zhou Jun's insistence. They were ordered to post bail and await further summons and interrogation.

Baoshan: Various Townships Telegraph Requests to Rectify Tax Deed Procedures 91

The various townships of this county telegraphed the Department of Finance requesting the rectification of deed tax procedures, stating, "Zhao Xunjian, Director of the Finance Department of Jiangsu Province: We, the people of Baoshan County, find that the county has long been promoting official deeds, using the various township offices as issuing points, which the people already find inconvenient. Since the establishment of the district system, it has become even more inconvenient for the people to buy and sell land, as the process is centralized in the district offices. For example, our district has a long and narrow terrain, with the various townships such as ChuanSha, YinBing, and DuChun in the northernmost part being as far as twenty li away. For the sale and purchase of even small plots of land, at least five or six people, including the seller, the buyer, and the witnesses, must travel back and forth more than forty li, and the road is rugged and difficult to travel. As a result, there are many people who write unofficial deeds with names such as 'preliminary official deed,' 'substitute,' or 'endorsement'. Even if people buy official deeds, it is difficult to investigate due to the long distance, and it is common for them to underreport the value of the deed. This is a major reason for the shortage of tax revenue. The Provincial Government Committee passed a resolution to allow the various townships to assist in the rectification of deed taxes and tasked them with handling this task. This would not only save the people the trouble of traveling back and forth, but it would also allow the various township leaders to conduct investigations nearby, which would be easier to clarify and prevent the above-mentioned abuses from occurring. The future of tax revenue will definitely make rapid progress, which is beneficial to both the national economy and the people's livelihood. This has already been ordered by your department in document number 2001, to be followed by the various counties. Now, the various counties have implemented this order, but Baoshan is alone in regretting that we have not done so. We cannot help but feel aggrieved. We have read the telegram from the county magistrate of Yixing County in your department's instructions, which states that the township offices directly promoting official deeds and assisting in deed taxes will facilitate procedures and increase administrative efficiency. We admire the intention of rectifying taxes. The township leaders believe that we should be treated equally and should not be divided. We have jointly submitted a request to the county magistrate of Baoshan County to implement this measure. We have received instructions from the county magistrate in documents number 245 and 9, stating that the matter of whether to change the county's method of promoting official deeds has been submitted to the Department of Finance for review. We respectfully inform you of this order. However, the people are eagerly awaiting this measure, and we dare to respectfully telegraph this request, hoping that you will investigate the case and order the county to implement it as soon as possible to appease the people's expectations and uphold the law. We are anxiously awaiting your order. Twenty township leaders, including Zhang Jianheng, the leader of Yuepu Township in the fifth district of Baoshan County, respectfully bow."

Changshu: Small Cart Driver Schemes to Capture Robber 92

The connecting express boat in Donglai Town of this county (which is towed by a steamer after reaching Beisha to Changshu) departed on the morning of the 19th. Suddenly, a passenger from another province, upon disembarking, immediately invited other passengers to play cards. Due to the lack of gambling tools on board, it was decided to abandon the idea. Unexpectedly, while collecting tickets on the boat as it passed Chenhang Bridge, the passenger produced a white Browning pistol and fired three shots into the air, then searched the passengers one by one, robbing them of all their silver dollars. Yu Youfu, an accounts collector from Tongrentai Pharmacy, was robbed of over a hundred yuan, the largest sum. He then disembarked at Caijia Bridge, intending to hire a cart to Xitang City. Unexpectedly, the cart driver he hailed had seen him robbing on the road in Chenhang the day before. The cart driver refused to hire his cart and let him walk alone. He then followed him secretly. Upon reaching Xitang City, he reported to the defense corps, who arrested the passenger and found a large amount of cash and a pistol hidden in his coat, as well as a patrol officer's badge from the 13th Water Police Team, but the badge only had the surname "Wang" and no first name. When questioned, the 13th team denied having such an officer. He was sent to the county government for interrogation on the 20th.

Business Tax Dispute Resolved 93

The local business tax bureau, due to the need to increase business tax rates and investigate the accounts of various shops, has encountered public opposition. As of the autumn tax payment deadline, not a single payment has been received. Director Huang once resigned. However, with the mediation of Pang Jiegong, chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, the expansion of the tax assessment has been cancelled, and it has been stated that similar disputes in other counties have been resolved. As the winter tax payment deadline is approaching, the bureau is also willing to make concessions, but the tax rates for the rice, silk, dried goods, groceries, and bean cake industries will be increased, while the rates for other industries will remain the same. It is reported that both parties have reached an agreement, and a formal resolution is expected soon.

Wuxi: Secret Den Manufacturing Poison Pills Smashed 94

The County Public Safety Bureau's Inspectorate, at approximately 4 PM of the day before yesterday, received a tip that the Yuebin Teahouse on Hanchang Road outside Guangfu Gate had a secret room manufacturing poison pills, specializing in fast-acting products for short-term highs, with brand names like "Champagne Three Masters" and "Golden Mouse," sold to various towns and villages in the city and countryside, generating huge profits. They requested a swift arrest. After receiving the tip, Inspector General Jin immediately dispatched inspectors Lu Chenggong and Sun Hao, leading an informant and police officers to the location. Upon arriving, they found a small room behind the teahouse with a false wall. A large glass cabinet was placed against the wall, and after opening the cabinet, a small door, large enough for one person to enter, was revealed. The door led to the second floor of the Huichuntang venereal disease doctor's office, which was the secret den for manufacturing poison pills. Fearing that the inspectors, under the guidance of the informant, would directly reach the secret room, they waited. At that time, twenty people were manufacturing the pills. They then carried out the arrest, seizing a machine for manufacturing poison pills, as well as drying racks, medicinal powder, and other raw materials, along with workers Jiang Longhai and Zhao Quanru, who were taken to the bureau for interrogation and detention. At the same time, a mahjong set and gamblers Wang Shuichang and others were seized in the teahouse and taken in for questioning. It is now reported that Inspector General Jin has identified the main culprits in the pill manufacturing as Cai and Lei, and many others, and is making every effort to investigate and bring them to justice.

Changzhou 95

Xinfu and Guohua Banks to Establish Branches in Changzhou

The banking industry in Wu County currently consists of five banks: China, Communications, Jiangsu, Shanghai Commercial & Savings, and Farmers Bank. It has been learned that the Xinfu and Guohua banks, in order to expand operations in Changzhou, have decided to establish branches in Changzhou in the shortest possible time. The managers of the two branches have already been appointed from experienced members of the local money exchange industry. Wang Jianchang will manage Xinfu, and Gu Shoutong will manage Guohua. They are currently preparing everything and should be able to open soon. In addition, the Changzhou branch of the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, in order to facilitate the exchange of remittances for various businesses in the western part of the city, has also decided to establish an office in Doushihe, which will begin operations on November 1.

Yangzhou: Ruthless Nephew Leaves Elderly Woman to Commit Suicide 96

In Toutiao Place of Lidian Township in the third district, an elderly widow, Wu, nearly seventy years old and with a violent temperament, had a son named Zhisong who worked as a farmer and lived in poverty. The woman had a nephew, Wu, who was relatively well-off and had taken care of her in her early years. The widow asked to borrow a room from his house to live in temporarily. Unexpectedly, the nephew did not agree. The old woman, in a fit of anger, became suicidal and used an iron tool to slit her own throat and die. The local township immediately reported it to the court, which sent people to inspect the body. After mediation, the son of the deceased, Zhisong, requested to waive the inspection.

Nantong: Seventh District Holds Village Clearing Campaign 97

The seventh district, consisting of Nantong, Rugao, Chongming, Haimen, and Qidong counties, has not yet quelled the bandit atmosphere. Commissioner Cheng convened a village clearing conference. To facilitate the search and suppression, each county was divided into a village clearing zone. A general supervisory department was established in Tong County, and the water and land military police teams within the territory were combined into a village clearing force, responsible for investigating and suppressing bandits and communists.

Bright Light: Hua Yu Firm's Ransom Victim Escapes Danger 98

Kao Shanzi, the youngest son of Li Chuanfa, the owner of Hua Yu Grain Store on North Main Street in this city, was kidnapped by the bandit Sun Wanlin and others last month. After many negotiations, nothing was achieved. Li then offered a reward of 500 yuan for his rescue. This time, the Sun bandits were dispersed by the militia near Gucheng. The guard then secretly stole Li's son from the bandit den and informed his family. Yesterday (the 18th) afternoon, they were reunited. The reunion of flesh and blood brought immense joy.

Fengyang Miaoshanpu Tobacco Farmers Robbed 99

Yesterday (the 16th), a dozen or so tobacco farmers sold tobacco to the British American Tobacco Company at Mentai, earning a total of 2400 yuan. That night, they stayed at a hotel owned by a Mr. Li in Miaoshanpu, forty-five miles from the county. Unexpectedly, more than twenty bandits suddenly arrived at night, carrying knives and searching everywhere, looting all the tobacco farmers' money.

Pinghu: Anti-Japanese Army Secretary Commits Suicide 100

Yu Nianci, the son of Yu Yunyan, the former principal of the First National School in this county, worked in a money shop. Recently, he joined a unit of the Northeast Volunteer Anti-Japanese Army as a secretary. Nianci had a beloved, named Quan Shangqing, the daughter of Xu Zuoquan Asheng of the county government. Since falling in love, he had spent thousands of yuan of family money. Four or five days ago, Nianci wanted to go to the Northeast again. When he arrived in Shanghai, he received a letter from a friend saying that his lover was having an affair with someone else. He returned home that night and found Shiqing playing with someone else, which led to a big conflict. Since Nianci had an affair with Shiqing, his family considered it a great disgrace and had long expelled him, forbidding him from entering the house. Now, facing further humiliation, he felt he had no way forward or backward and swallowed opium to commit suicide. When the poison took effect, he was turned away from several places. In the end, a friend helped him to Quan Asheng's house, where he died. This serves as a profound lesson for those who fall into depravity in their youth.

Jiashan: Unrest in Dingjiazhai Due to Bandits 101

Since the failure to suppress bandits in Dingjiazhai in the county, the bandits have become bolder, gathering in the Jinze Niduantou area. They rob along the road in groups of two or three from time to time, causing disturbances everywhere. Although the Seventh Water Police Team has been tracking and suppressing them, it has been futile because the bandits are extremely familiar with the waterways and harbors, appearing and disappearing unpredictably. Suppression is particularly difficult. It is now learned that County Magistrate Huang of this county and the captain of the Qingpu Jinshui Marine Police Team have negotiated a joint defense plan. The county and Qingpu water police will deploy elite troops, increase firearms, and form special joint teams to be stationed there permanently, patrolling daily. In addition, the Yaozhuang Bridge and Yuhui base teams will be temporarily placed under their command. Furthermore, to eliminate local ruffians, a six-month clearing campaign will continue to be carried out.

Hangzhou: Shanghai-Hangzhou Express Train Kills Villager 102

At the Jianqiao Railway Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, at around 10 a.m. on the 19th, a villager named Wang Ashun was walking on the tracks. Unexpectedly, the Shanghai-Hangzhou express train departed from Hangzhou city and, passing through the area, Wang failed to avoid it and was crushed to death. The scene was a bloody mess, too horrible to bear. The local police station reported it to the court for inspection, and the body was prepared for burial. The deceased was 41 years old and from Yiqiao, Xiaoshan. He left behind a young son and daughter, and their situation is extremely difficult. The railway bureau has provided a consolation payment of twenty yuan.

Robbery Occurs in Jianqiao Last Night 103

At Shenjiatang, about half a mile from Jianqiao in Hangzhou, at around 6 p.m. on the 19th, two robbers suddenly came to the home of a resident named Qiu Delin. Each carried a pistol. One robber stood guard outside the door, while the other, wearing a long blue cloth gown, entered to rob. Qiu's daughter had recently married and had just returned home from her husband's family. The robbers threatened the father and daughter to hand over their money and ordered them to remove the gold ring from her hand. By accident, she dropped it into the pond, and it could not be found. The robber angrily fired a shot, wounding the woman in the foot. The bullet passed through the back of her foot. The robbers then swaggered away. The police were notified and pursued them, but to no avail. The injured person was sent to the hospital for treatment.

Xiaoshan: Anti-Japanese Association Seizes Large Quantity of Enemy Goods 104

On the 18th, inspectors from the Xiaoshan Anti-Japanese Association seized a cloth boat carrying goods to Kai and Shaoxing in front of Huiqiao in the urban area. Inside were more than seventy pieces of Japanese floral velvet cloth, shipped from the Maolong Cloth Shop in Hangzhou to Dasheng and Santai Cloth in Shaoxing. The goods were seized, and after inspection confirmed that they were Japanese goods, they were sent to the association for review.

Hefei: Zhang Guangjian Accused of Fraud 105

The Shenfu Money Shop on East Main Street in Hefei went bankrupt with more than 200,000 yuan in debt. Among the shareholders of the shop was Zhang Guangdai's son, Xie Sheng, the son of the former military governor of Gansu, Zhang Guangjian. He had borrowed more than 100,000 yuan in principal and interest from the Shanghai Taiping Bank by mortgaging the shop's assets. The Taiping Bank sent a representative, Xiang Shiquan, and the Shenfu Money Shop, with the approval of the local court, seized Zhang's residence and fields. The former military governor of Gansu, Zhang Guangjian, suddenly hired lawyer Xia Chongrang from Pingxiangli, claiming that Zhang Xie Sheng was his adopted son and had no right to mortgage his property. The Taiping Bank and the Shenfu Money Shop then accused Zhang Guangjian of fraud in court. In addition to defending himself, Zhang also telegraphed various authorities, explaining the situation. Li Mugong, director of the Taiping Bank, has now joined forces with the Shanghai Banking Association, Money Industry Association, and Chamber of Commerce to deal with the matter seriously and will telegraph the entire country.

Local News: Chen Wenlin Flies Jiang Que Aircraft to Hangzhou Yesterday Afternoon 106

Pan Dingxin, Mechanic Wang Shenghai Staying in Shanghai, Accompanies Him

Zeng Yijing and Others See Them Off at Hongqiao Airport

Chen Wenlin, Director of the Xiamen Naval Aviation Department, and Pan Dingxin, Head of the Mechanical Section, flew the domestically produced Jiang Que aircraft from Shanghai to Hangzhou yesterday afternoon, before continuing to Xiamen to complete their national flight feat. People from all walks of life saw them off at Hongqiao Airport. The details are as follows:

Flying Yesterday Afternoon 107

The Jiang Que aircraft, departing from Xiamen, passed through Nanjing, Xuzhou, Jinan, Tianjin, Beijing, and Hankou before returning to Shanghai and landing at Hongqiao Airport. It was equipped with a new 120-horsepower British Hansman engine. After test flying, it proved excellent. At 10 a.m. yesterday morning, Chen Wenlin and Wang Shenghai, a mechanic from the Xiamen Aviation Department staying in Shanghai, arrived at Hongqiao Airport. They first inspected the fuselage. At 12 o'clock, Chen Wenlin piloted the aircraft himself, with Wang Shenghai as a passenger, and took off. As for Pan Dingxin, Head of the Mechanical Section, he remained in Shanghai due to an eye ailment and decided to take a sea liner to Xiamen instead.

Farewell from All Circles 108

Those who saw them off at Hongqiao Airport yesterday included Chen Xunyong, Commander of the Naval Training Fleet, Zeng Yijing, Director of the Aircraft Manufacturing Department, engineer Wang Chonghong, Chen Zaofan, Deputy Director of the Jiangnan Shipyard, Lin Wojang of the Aviation Association, and relatives of Chen Wenlin. After Chen boarded the plane, he first circled in the sky to show his gratitude to those who came to see him off. At 12:15 p.m., he finally left Shanghai. The plane arrived in Hangzhou at 1 p.m. that day, landing at Jianqiao Airport, and visited the aviation school. This morning, it will take off from Hangzhou again, passing through Ningbo to reach Fuzhou. Tomorrow morning, it will fly back from Fuzhou to Xiamen for a short rest to handle important documents from the Aviation Department. Then, it will fly from Xiamen to South China to complete the national flight plan.

The Ministry of Industry Sends Personnel to Shanghai 114

To Investigate the Electric Power Strike and the Workers' Donation of Salaries

The Electric Power Company dismissed Chinese workers without cause and refused to pay pensions, which led to a joint strike of 1,700 Chinese employees. Although most of the employees have resumed work, 1,400 workers and 30 Chinese staff members are still firmly continuing the strike, and the situation is serious.

Ministry Officials Investigate 115

A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency in Beijing learned from the Ministry of Industry yesterday that the ministry considers this case to be important and has specially dispatched Bao Guohua, a section chief from the Labor Department, to Shanghai to investigate the truth and assist the local competent authorities in handling the matter in order to eliminate the dispute.

Labor Circles Provide Assistance 116

During this strike by the electric power workers, the labor circles in the city generally believe that the company's handling of the situation was inappropriate, so they have expressed their support. Yesterday, the six district water and electricity trade unions again sent representatives Ding Kunshan, Shao Yubao, Chen Housui, and Wu Shunfu to express their condolences and donated one day's wages for all the workers, totaling 319 yuan and 81 cents. The four district electrical appliance trade union also sent representative Cai Zhengkang to express condolences and provided assistance of 23 yuan and 70 cents, encouraging them to do their best to struggle. The electric power workers were extremely excited by this assistance and all expressed their determination to fight to the end.

The Capital Ferry Will Hold Opening Ceremony in Nanjing Tomorrow Morning 117

The two railway bureaus will be represented by Zheng Baozhao

Appointed receptionists to take care of them along the way

The Ministry of Railways Invites All Circles to Visit

The Capital Yangtze River Ferry will hold its opening ceremony in Nanjing tomorrow morning and will begin operating on the same day. The details were published in yesterday's newspaper. The Ministry of Railways previously issued 500 invitations through the Jinpu and Jinghu Railways to invite all circles to Nanjing to attend the ceremony. At the same time, Zheng Baozhao, the director of the Traffic Department of the Jinghu Railway Bureau, will prepare eight or nine passenger cars at the Xiaguan Station in Nanjing on the morning of the 22nd to accommodate the guests. As soon as the guests arrive, they will be seated and depart for the Meihuigang Ferry Terminal at 9:30 a.m. The guests will disembark from the mobile stairs and board the ferry. Three steel cars will be prepared to be driven onto the ferry. After arriving at Pukou Terminal, the steel cars will be driven ashore and then driven back. The opening ceremony will be held on the ferry at that time. Photographs and moving pictures will be taken to commemorate the event. A reception desk will be set up at the Xiaguan Station, with Zhou Xisan, section chief of the Ministry of Railways' Affairs Department, serving as the chief receptionist. The security of the venue will be the responsibility of the Jinpu and Jinghu Railway Police Departments and the Capital Constabulary. Two Boy Scouts will be hired to serve on the ferry. As for the reception of people from all walks of life along the way, Director Zheng Baozhao of the Jinghu Railway Affairs Department will be in charge of everything. At the same time, the Jinghu Railway Bureau has specially appointed Zheng to go to Nanjing by early train this morning to participate in the opening ceremony. Zheng has also specially commissioned Xu Chaoyuan, deputy chief of the Jinghu section, as the director of the Jinghu reception, with Wang Shuchun and Tang Huannan as deputy directors, to preside over the reception on the train and on the train. Zou Zhengjian, Chen Faxiang, Chen Yi, Li Songbai, Chen Ligang, and others have been appointed as train receptionists and will also go to Beijing with Zheng this morning. Sun Baiying, a specialist from the Ministry of Railways, will serve as the master of ceremonies at the venue. However, the ribbon-cutting ceremony is still being arranged by Zeng Zhongming, the vice minister of railways. It is expected that President Wang will officiate. The order of the opening ceremony on that day is recorded below: (1) The train departs from Xiaguan Station to Meihuigang Ferry Terminal; (2) Guests disembark and board the Yangtze River ferry, the ferry plays music; (3) Meeting begins; (4) Sing the Party song; (5) Bow three times to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the Prime Minister; (6) The chairman respectfully reads the Prime Minister's will; (7) Chairman's speech (Ministry Vice Minister); (8) Report by the director of the Ferry Engineering Office; (9) Admonition and speeches by guests; (10) Ribbon-cutting ceremony, music plays; (11) Steel car drives onto the ferry (11 a.m.); (12) Departure; (13) Steel car lands at Pukou; (14) Ferry returns to Meihuigang; (15) Guests disembark; (16) Guests board the train for tea and snacks; (17) Train returns to Xiaguan Station; (18) Ceremony ends.
