Shanghai-Beiping Through Train Starts Tomorrow 119

The Ministry of Railways Formulates Service Rules for Chief Inspectors

Temporarily Fixed Fees for Various Railway Materials Crossing the River

Yesterday's Instructions to the Two Railway Bureau Administrations to Comply

The Shanghai-Beiping through train on the Jinghu, Jinpu and Beining lines will start running on the 22nd. The Ministry of Railways has specially formulated service rules for chief inspectors traveling on the through train, detailed rules for handling Shanghai-Beiping through trains, and has established fees for various railway materials to cross the river by ferry. Yesterday, the two railway bureau administrations were instructed to comply. The original text is explored and recorded below:

River Crossing Fees for Railway Materials 120

Yesterday, the railway department issued instructions to the railway bureau stating: "In view of the fact that the Ministry's Capital Ferry's river crossing fees for various types of goods have been established and announced, and all lines have been ordered to comply, as for various railway materials such as locomotives, coal water cars, passenger cars, freight cars, etc., page 94 of the freight classification table does not specify a grade. To calculate the river crossing fee for the above ferries, the grades are temporarily fixed as follows in order to collect the river crossing fee according to the grades: (1) Locomotives, coal water cars, flower cars, chartered cars, first-class cars, first and second-class mixed cars, etc., and similar vehicles should be charged the river crossing fee according to the actual weight of each vehicle and compared to the first class; (2) Second, third, and fourth class passenger cars, guard cars, luggage cars, official cars, and various freight cars, etc., should be charged the river crossing fee according to the actual weight of each vehicle and compared to the third class; (3) Other railway materials for which grades have already been established should be charged the river crossing fee according to their original grades. In addition to notification, you must immediately comply and implement this order."

Service Rules for Chief Inspectors 121

Service rules for chief inspectors traveling with the through train of the Joint Transportation Department of the Ministry of Railways: (1) The chief inspector of the through train is under the command of the director of the Joint Transportation Department and is responsible for inspecting, supervising, and communicating all joint transportation matters related to the through train. (2) The shifts of the chief inspector traveling on the through train are assigned by the Joint Transportation Department. Any changes not approved by the Joint Transportation Department are not allowed, and they must not leave their posts without authorization. (3) When the chief inspector is on duty on the assigned train, in addition to carrying joint transportation regulations and various notices related to the through train, they must also carry the chief inspector service certificate issued by the Joint Transportation Department. However, this service certificate is only valid for riding the train during the assigned shift. If they ride other trains, they will be treated as riding without a ticket, and the lines they pass through will charge for the ticket according to the regulations. (4) Each time the through train's chief inspector must report the entire situation of the through train in person to the Joint Transportation Department after the train arrives in Jingnan and the shift is changed. (5) Whether the through train's vehicles are complete when crossing the rails should be carefully inspected by employees assigned by the joint transportation line and the chief inspector traveling with the train. After preparing and signing the report, they should be submitted separately to the Joint Transportation Department and the Traffic Department of the relevant line for review. (6) Regarding tickets, berths, luggage, parcels, reception, hygiene, and all other matters related to the through train, the chief inspector may correct any facts that are not in accordance with the regulations or are inappropriate at any time and report them separately to the Joint Transportation Department and the Traffic Department of the relevant line. (7) When an accident occurs on the through train en route, the chief inspector traveling with the train should assist the relevant officials of the line where the accident occurred in handling it and report it to the Joint Transportation Department for the record. (8) In order to understand the situation of the through train, the Joint Transportation Department will prepare a separate inspection report form, which the chief inspector will fill out in detail each time they are on duty and submit it to the Joint Transportation Department for the record. (9) Each joint transportation line's notices, telegrams, or transportation matters related to the joint transportation should be copied and sent to the chief inspectors by the traffic department of the joint transportation line at any time. (10) If there are any matters not covered in these rules, the Joint Transportation Department may submit a request to amend them at any time. (11) These rules will take effect from the date of approval.

Shanghai-Beiping Through Train Operation Rules 122

The following are the operational rules for the Shanghai-Beiping through train service on the Jinghu, Jinpu, and Beining Railways, as ordered by the Ministry of Railways to facilitate travel between Shanghai and Beiping. Article 1: The Shanghai-Beiping direct through train service on the Jinghu, Jinpu, and Beining Railways, as ordered by the Ministry of Railways, is established for the convenience of passengers traveling between Shanghai and Beiping, and is abbreviated as the Shanghai-Beiping Through Train. Article 2: The Shanghai-Beiping Through Train will run once daily from Shanghai and Beiping in opposite directions, designated as Train 301 and Train 302. The arrival and departure times at the main stations are as follows: Train 301 departs from Beiping at 7:15 AM, arrives at Tianjin at 10:35 AM, departs at 11:00 AM, arrives at Jinan at 8:50 PM, departs at 9:10 PM, arrives at Xuzhou at 6:00 AM, departs at 6:20 AM, arrives at Pukou at 3:05 PM, departs from Nanjing at 5:25 PM, and arrives at Shanghai at 11:55 PM. Train 302 departs from Shanghai at 12:00 AM, arrives at Nanjing at 7:45 AM, departs from Pukou at 11:00 AM, arrives at Xuzhou at 8:12 PM, departs at 8:22 PM, arrives at Jinan at 7:00 AM, departs at 7:30 AM, arrives at Tianjin at 5:00 PM, departs at 5:35 PM, and arrives at Beiping at 8:48 PM. Article 3: Each Shanghai-Beiping Through Train will consist of ten carriages as a general principle, but between Pukou and Beiping, one sleeping car from the Wagons-Lits Company is permitted. Between Shanghai and Nanjing, if passenger traffic is heavy, one first-class or second-class passenger car may be added as appropriate. The composition is as follows: one fourth-class sleeping car, one first-class saloon car, one first-class dining car, two second-class sleeping cars, three third-class passenger cars, one baggage car, one guard/mail car, and one Wagons-Lits Company sleeping car (temporarily allowed between Beiping and Pukou). Article 4: The Shanghai-Beiping Through Train should use blue steel cars as much as possible. Article 5: Seven trains should be prepared for the Shanghai-Beiping Through Train. The allocation method is as follows: based on the mileage ratio of each route, Jinpu will provide five trains, Jinghu will provide slightly more than one train, and Beining will provide less than one train. However, for mutual assistance and to maintain orderly management and convenience, Jinghu and Beining Railways should each provide one train. All extra trains provided by Beining will not be charged rental fees to Jinghu. Article 6: The trains provided by each route should not be interchanged as a general principle. Article 7: These seven trains will operate with five trains, with one train undergoing minor repairs at the workshops of the providing route in rotation, and another train undergoing major repairs in rotation. The order and dates of all major and minor repairs should be carried out in accordance with the attached schedule. If the two Beining and Jinghu trains are scheduled for major and minor repairs within the same period, the scheduled minor repair time for the Beining or Jinghu train should be advanced by one minor repair cycle. If the same train is scheduled for major and minor repairs within the same period, the scheduled minor repair for that train should be canceled, and the remaining trains should be advanced by one minor repair cycle accordingly. Furthermore, major repairs for each train should be carried out according to the attached schedule. If there are changes to the order of minor repairs, the department may consult with the relevant routes at any time as necessary. Article 8: The operation of the dining car on each train will be managed by the providing route. Article 9: Each train carriage should be equipped with necessary items, such as bedding, and consumable items, such as soap, towels, sanitary water, and brooms, which should be provided by the providing route. The expenses for these consumable items and the laundry costs for bedding will be listed monthly by Jinghu and Beining and submitted to the Through Transportation Department of the Ministry of Railways via Jinpu, and will be paid from the sleeper car revenue. Article 10: The costs of operating materials, such as staff salaries, coal, water, oil, and cotton waste, will be borne by each route, except for oil, water, and cotton waste, which should be provided by the route through which the train is passing as much as possible. Article 11: After the train arrives at the terminal station, the cleaning of the exterior and underside of all passenger cars will be the responsibility of the arriving route, and no additional costs will be shared by other routes. Article 12: If a train provided by Route A is damaged while operating on Route B, Route B should temporarily provide a replacement car and notify Route A by telegram. When the next train returns to Route A, Route A should prepare a replacement car and exchange it for the car provided by Route B, which will then be attached to the original train to return to Route B. However, if Jinpu is in the middle of the route and a train provided by Jinpu is damaged on Jinghu or Beining, in addition to the respective passing route temporarily providing a replacement car, Jinpu should also be notified immediately so that Jinpu can prepare another car to be attached when the train passes through that route, and the replacement car attached by Jinghu or Beining can be exchanged upon arrival at Shanghai or Beiping, to avoid passengers having to change trains mid-journey. Article 13: If a train provided by Route A is damaged on Route B, Route B should provide free minor repairs, but the cost of materials should be borne by the providing route. For major repairs, the train should be sent back to the original providing route for self-repair. If it cannot be transported back to the providing route, the providing route should send materials to Route B for repair, and the transportation of materials and the round-trip travel of workers on Route B should be free of charge. Article 14: The train should not be handed over to Route B with a damaged car at the connecting station. If a damaged car is found, Route A should repair it or replace it with a good car before handing it over, unless the damaged car was originally handed over by Route B. Article 15: The Shanghai-Beiping Through Train should primarily sell through tickets. The sale of short-distance tickets within sections should be the responsibility of the traffic departments of each passing route, and should not exceed the number of seats in each class of carriage. Article 16: The allocation of berths on this train is as follows: the originating route receives 60%, and the transit route receives 40%, which should be managed centrally by each route and not distributed to each ticket office. Article 17: (1) The berth tickets for Train 301 and Train 302 should use the ordinary berth ticket format, with an additional printed red diagonal cross, and should be handled by the issuing station and transferred to the through transportation department by the accounting departments of each route in accordance with the sales method for through tickets. All revenue from berth tickets, after deducting the train operating expenses and bedding laundry costs specified in Article 9, should be distributed according to the mileage of each route (the mileage distribution method is based on the instructions of the Through Transportation Department's telegraph). (2) The supplementary berth tickets and capital ferry fees collected by the ticket inspectors on Train 301 and Train 302 (supplementary tickets for passengers traveling beyond class, beyond station, or without a ticket should still use the supplementary ticket formats of each route) should use the supplementary ticket format and reporting methods as follows: (A) Use light yellow, segmented tickets for supplementary payments. (B) The ticket inspector must prepare a report and submit it to the station master to be sent to the accounting department for storage and transfer. Article 18: The service staff on each train, such as baggage clerks, car attendants, electricians, car inspectors, dining car cooks, and attendants, should be assigned by the providing route and travel directly with the train, but the providing route should notify the other two routes of the names and numbers of the aforementioned staff for their record. The train conductor (or passenger traffic inspector), car conductor, ticket inspector, coupler, police officer, and security team should change shifts at the connecting station. However, between Pukou and Nanjing, the on-duty car conductor of the receiving route should cross the river to hand over to the off-duty car conductor. Article 19: In addition to being managed by their respective providing routes, the service staff on each train should also be under the command of the supervisors of each passing route. If any dereliction of duty or inappropriate handling of matters occurs on the passing route, the relevant department of the passing route may review the situation and notify the providing route for disciplinary action. Article 20: The water used by the carriages on each train should be supplied free of charge by each passing route as much as possible to avoid shortages. Article 21: The heating needed by each train in winter, in addition to being supplied by the locomotive, should be fully supplied by the two terminal stations when the train is parked at the terminals. At the major stations in the middle, when the locomotive is detached from the train, the major stations should also have preparations for supplying heating. Article 22: Commonly damaged parts on each train, such as (1) various springs, (2) various spring iron pieces and screws, (3) steel tiles, brake shoes, and cotter pins, should be pre-stored in a wooden box in each guard car by the providing route for temporary use. Article 23: The expenses specified in these operational rules should be allocated by each route along with the ticket price on a regular basis and should not be delayed. Article 24: Matters not specified in these operational rules should be handled in accordance with the through transportation regulations. Article 25: These operational rules will be effective from the date of the start of through train service. If there are any outstanding matters, they may be amended by agreement of the three routes.

Page 13

Grain Industry Discusses Sending Personnel to Thoroughly Investigate the Shipment of Japanese and American Rice to Shanghai; Municipal Chamber of Commerce Also Sends Letters of Admonishment, Urging Compliance with Agreements and Fulfillment of Civic Duty 123

Eight rice shops in the Nanshi area of this port, including Shenfeng, have purchased 20,050 bags of small-grain rice. Rumors circulate in the market that this rice is of Japanese origin, and the Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai has sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce requesting strict measures to prevent the sale of this rice in order to protect domestic agriculture. It is reported that the Grain Industry Association, in order to clarify the true situation, also convened a meeting of its members the day before yesterday, resolving to appoint Fang Yusheng and Chen Shide to conduct a thorough investigation. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has also sent letters to both the soybean and rice industries to investigate and admonish their members to fulfill their patriotic duties as merchants. The details of the investigation are recorded below.

Letter to the Soybean and Rice Industries: The Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai has sent a letter to this Chamber reporting the dumping of aged rice from Japanese warehouses in Shanghai. According to reports, this Japanese rice has now arrived in Shanghai and is stored in Yongxing Warehouse, to be sold by eight rice shops in Nanshi, including Shenfeng. This matter is related to obstructing domestic agricultural production and violating boycott agreements. Your association has the responsibility to supervise and investigate, and cannot ignore it. Please conduct a strict and confidential investigation and, if it is confirmed, impose sanctions according to regulations. This is our sincere request.

Letter to the Rice Shops: This Chamber has previously received a letter from the Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai stating that Japan intends to sell over one million stones of stored rice, with the first batch of 25,000 bags already shipped. According to reports, this first batch of Japanese rice has already arrived in Shanghai warehouses and is said to be sold by eight rice shops in Nanshi, including Shenfeng. In addition to sending a letter to the Rice Shop Association for strict investigation and handling, this matter is related to obstructing domestic agricultural production and violating warehouse goods agreements. Your association must admonish its members to refuse to trade and maintain a strict defense, so as not to be taken advantage of by the enemy, and to fulfill their patriotic duties as merchants. Please provide a written report of your compliance.

Grain Industry Meeting: The Grain, Oil, and Cake Association convened a meeting of its members on the afternoon of the day before yesterday, with three to four hundred people in attendance. Only three of the eight shops, including Shenfeng, Changmao, Dafeng, and Dingtai, were present. The attending members requested that the association summon the five absent shops, but they still did not arrive after being summoned. The Guangdong faction sternly questioned and interrogated the chairman as to whether the association knew that these eight shops were selling Japanese rice, and stated that these eight shops were reputable and should not violate the resolutions. Subsequently, the members all said that selling Japanese rice was only for personal gain, and the outside world was discussing it, causing the members to suffer. If strict measures were not taken, the members would refuse to associate with these eight shops. After discussion by the committee members, it was decided that the case should first clarify whether the rice was shipped by a Japanese ship or a Western ship. Fang Yusheng and Chen Shide were appointed as investigators and should immediately investigate. If it is confirmed that the rice was shipped by a Japanese ship, the profits from the sale of the rice will be used for charitable purposes. All the rice purchased by the eight shops, including Shenfeng, will be temporarily kept by this association. Only after obtaining the consent of the members will Fang and Chen be allowed to take on the investigation. The members then dispersed.

Grain Industry Announcement: This is an announcement regarding the receipt of a letter from the Ningxian Rice Shop and Warehouse Association stating that a large quantity of Japanese rice has arrived in Shanghai and that rumors circulate in the market that a large amount has been purchased. We have also received letters from Shen Shouzhang and the Yuantang Grain Shop Association of the Quanzhang Guild Hall stating the same. Based on this, an emergency meeting of the executive committee was convened on October 19, resolving to investigate. The eight shops purchased 25,000 bags of small-grain rice, and rumors circulate in the market that this rice is of Japanese origin. According to Chengjin, a member of the industry, the goods were purchased from the American trading company Handao Lai, and are goods delivered from the warehouse. The focus of this case should first clarify whether the goods were shipped by a Japanese ship or a Western ship, which is the prerequisite for resolving this case. It was resolved that the small-grain rice purchased by the eight shops should be temporarily kept by this association, and the true nature of the goods should be investigated. Fang Yusheng and Chen Shide were immediately appointed as investigators to conduct a thorough investigation. If it is confirmed that the rice was shipped by a Japanese ship, the profits from the future sale of the rice will be used by this association for charitable purposes, and the losses will be borne by the eight shops. If it is found that the rice was shipped by a Western ship, the profits should be returned to the Chengjin members. However, only three of the eight shops were present at today's meeting, and consent was obtained from them. If the remaining five shops express dissent, it will be discussed again. It is also noted that domestic agricultural production has been bountiful in recent years, and rice prices have plummeted. The fundamental way to rescue rural areas is to boycott the dumping of foreign rice. Therefore, members should refuse to buy and sell Japanese rice from Japanese merchants. As for goods from Western merchants, this association should also advise members to temporarily stop ordering and strive to rescue agriculture together. These are the matters recorded and announced, and it is hoped that all members of the association will be informed.

Public Indignation at the End of the Meeting: When the meeting was adjourned, a broker nicknamed "Old Bibao" was walking from the third floor to the second-floor market when he was scolded by the members, who called him a traitor. This led to a quarrel, and teapots and teacups were thrown all over the market. People later persuaded them to disperse. After Shenfeng and the other eight shops violated the Grain Industry Association's resolution and sold a large quantity of Japanese rice, outsiders questioned them. Yesterday morning, slogans expressing indignation were posted all over Doushi Street and in front of the shops.

Wen Yuqing Discusses International Telecommunications; Zhenru New Radio Station to Be Completed Soon; Press to Be Invited for Tour on 23rd 124

A Central News Agency reporter visited Wen Yuqing, Director of the International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, yesterday morning to inquire about the report from the Japanese Rengo News Agency regarding the Chinese government's cancellation of the Shuangqiao Radio Station contract. The reply was as follows:

Shuangqiao Radio Station Contract 125

In 1918, the Navy Department of the Beijing government signed a contract with the Japanese Mitsui & Co. for the Shuangqiao Radio Station. The contract stipulated the construction of a long-wave radio station in Beiping. The station was built many years ago but has not yet been put into operation. As for the Tokyo dispatch from the Japanese Rengo News Agency that the Chinese government has cancelled this contract, causing the Japanese Foreign Ministry to demand 5 million yuan in construction fees, I have not heard of this. The cancellation of this contract and the related negotiations should be handled jointly by the Ministries of Foreign Affairs, Navy, and Communications.

Sino-British Telecommunications to Be Realized on New Year's Day 126

Preparations for the International Telecommunications Bureau to establish Sino-British telecommunications are actively underway. One transmitter has already arrived in Shanghai and its assembly has been completed. Another transmitter is expected to arrive in Shanghai within two weeks. Once it arrives, it will be transported to Zhenru for installation. The exact date for the start of Sino-British telecommunications is set for New Year's Day next year. The students sent by the Ministry of Communications to study radio in England will be reporting to the bureau for service soon.

Zhenru Radio Station to Be Completed Soon 127

Wen also mentioned that international telecommunications have already been established with Germany, France, Russia, Italy, the United States, and the Netherlands. Telecommunications with Hong Kong are expected to be realized within the year. In order to expedite telecommunications between Shanghai and Hong Kong, an engineer was recently sent to Shanghai to inspect the equipment at the Hong Kong radio station. The bureau is completing the Zhenru New Radio Station, and has therefore scheduled to invite the domestic press to tour the new project next Monday (the 23rd) at 2:30 PM.

Plans to Establish International Wireless Telephone Service 128

It is also learned that the bureau plans to establish an international wireless telephone service to facilitate international calls and is planning to purchase equipment. The cost will not be high, as some of the existing equipment can be reused and only secret voice transmitters need to be purchased. All plans are currently under discussion.

Reorganization of the Shanghai Savings and Remittance Bureau 129

Internal Implementation Already Underway; Official Cancellation on New Year's Day

Since the establishment of the Postal Economic System Research Committee, the reorganization of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau under the Postal Administration has been discussed repeatedly. A draft plan was submitted by the committee to the Executive Yuan for discussion at the Central Political Conference. The principle of merging has been decided, and the relevant agencies are preparing for the merger procedures. For the sake of consolidation, the Ministry of Communications has ordered the Shanghai Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau to merge its operations with the Postal Administration. A Central News Agency reporter inquired about this with the person in charge of the bureau, and received the following response:

Merger 130

According to the person in charge, the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau was originally directly under the Ministry of Communications, with branches established in Shanghai, Hankou, and Tianjin, and savings and remittance offices attached to post offices in various locations. Recently, the Central Government decided to reorganize the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau under the Postal Administration. Currently, the merger procedures are still taking time and may not be realized soon. For the sake of consolidation, the Ministry of Communications has ordered the Shanghai Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau to merge its operations with the Postal Administration. Internal implementation of the merger and consolidation is already underway. However, due to accounting and other reasons, the official cancellation of the Shanghai Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau will be at the end of the year. All operations are still being conducted as usual and are not affected in the slightest.

Announcement 131

The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau announces that the issue of the reorganization of this bureau under the Postal Administration has been decided by the Central Political Conference. All regulations are currently being reviewed and will be implemented after being formulated and promulgated in accordance with legislative procedures. We have received an order from the Ministry of Communications to first abolish the Shanghai Savings and Remittance Bureau and merge all operations with this bureau in order to achieve economy and demonstrate consolidation. Except for internal affairs, the merger has already been implemented in accordance with the order. However, due to accounting and other reasons, the name of the Shanghai Savings and Remittance Bureau will be cancelled from January 1, year 23 [1934]. From that date onwards, all external operations will continue to be conducted directly under the name of this bureau. As for the tickets, seals, deposit slips, etc. used, as the names may change after the reorganization to avoid repeated modifications, everything will be used as before. This is a special announcement.

Postal Workers' Indignation Towards Liu and Yang 132

Sparks Urgent Postal Workers' Movement to Recover Savings and Remittance Bureau

According to news from the two postal workers' unions, the former directors of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, Liu Shufan and Yang Jianping, were found to be derelict of duty and corrupt in office, embezzling large sums of money. The Control Yuan has filed an impeachment, and the court is conducting a public prosecution. The two postal workers' unions advocate strict punishment and urge the government to recover the Savings and Remittance Bureau to prevent future problems. Yesterday, important committee members of the two postal workers' unions claimed that the discovery of the Liu and Yang corruption case was a great misfortune for society. We cannot condone Liu and Yang and sincerely hope that the Control Yuan and the judiciary will handle the case impartially and give them the punishment they deserve under the law to maintain the government's credibility. However, in terms of solidifying postal savings and remittance, this is only a palliative measure. If we want the position of postal savings to be permanently solid and prevent the continued discovery of corruption cases, there is no other way than to thoroughly recover the Savings and Remittance Bureau. Only by merging the Savings and Remittance Bureau into the Postal Administration can the business operate soundly and the public's confidence be established. Otherwise, the collapse of the postal savings and remittance business can be expected to happen soon. Since the Savings and Remittance Bureau was established separately, all the measures taken by the bureau have been contrary to the practices of postal personnel in terms of system and spirit. The errors are too great to bear to speak of. The Liu and Yang corruption is only one example. If the government does not make a decisive decision soon, the money invested may be lost. A reporter inquired about the news reported yesterday that the Ministry of Communications has ordered the abolition of the Shanghai Savings and Remittance Bureau and asked about the union's attitude towards this news. The reply was that although it is somewhat late, the fact that the Ministry of Communications can make a decisive decision at this time can also be seen as the authorities' quick stop to the situation, which we are happy to hear. However, the news of the Savings and Remittance Bureau's merger has been announced more than once, and we hope that the authorities will show the facts to the public as soon as possible.

Chen Qinglu, Employee of Shanghai Power Company, Suddenly Assassinated Yesterday Morning 133

Three Assailants Lay in Wait Near Chen's Residence

First Taken to Yinxing Port and Then Forced into a Car to Shijia浜

Six or Seven Shots Fired; Chen Hit by Three Bullets and His Life in Danger

City Police Authorities Intensively Searching for the Murderers

At around 10 AM yesterday morning, an assassination occurred at Shijia浜 on Mayushan Road, Yinxing Port, in Pudong. The victim was Chen Qinglu, an employee of the Shanghai Power Company. During the recent labor unrest at the company, employees contacted workers to strike in order to pressure the company to recognize the workers' demands. However, in recent days, many employees have gradually returned to work due to pressure from the company. Chen was one of those who voluntarily returned to work, which made him resented by some parties. Yesterday morning at 9 AM, assassins were secretly sent to ambush Chen at the location and shot him with handguns, intending to murder him. The injured person was found by patrol officer Zhang Yulong of the Fourth Precinct of the Fifth District, who took him to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment. It is said that his life is in danger. The details of the investigation are recorded below:

[P] Chen's Family Background

Chen Rongqing, a local resident, is 65 years old and runs a cotton-fluffing shop called Chen Wanxing in Houjia浜 in the city. He lives at No. 24 in Beizhangjia Lane. His wife, Li, is 67 years old and has two sons and a daughter. The eldest son, Chen Qingfu, is 33 years old and works as an employee at the Shanghai Power Company. His wife, Wang, is 28 years old and has a son and a daughter. The son is named Maotou and is 4 years old, and the daughter is named Peijuan and is 9 years old. The second child is a daughter, Chen Huizhen, who is 30 years old and married to a man surnamed Li. The youngest child is a son, Chen Qinglu, who is currently 22 years old. He was introduced to the Shanghai Power Company by his elder brother and has been working as an employee in the materials department for many years. With the support of his parents, he was engaged to a woman surnamed Jin through a matchmaker, but they have not yet married. The family of several people has a fairly comfortable life.

Sudden Encounter with Assailants 134

At around 8 AM yesterday morning, Chen Qinglu left home as usual and hired a rickshaw to go to the Shanghai Power Company at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Jiangxi Road to work. However, before he had gone far, three assailants wearing blue short shirts and pants stopped the rickshaw and ordered him to get out, saying that they wanted to talk to him at a certain labor union in the Jiangye Guild Hall on Fuyou Road. He was forced to get out of the rickshaw and walk to the guild hall. After sitting there for about 20 minutes, the assailants suddenly told Chen that they wanted to talk to a certain organization at Yinxing Port. Although Chen was unwilling, he could not do anything. He then went out of the guild hall with the assailants. At this time, the assailants had already called Yunfei Motor Company and hired a car with license number 12323, which was parked in front of the guild hall. The driver, Jin Ronghua, did not pay attention, but saw Chen get into the car with the assailants. Then, under the direction of the assailants, the car sped to Shijia浜 on Mayushan Road, Yinxing Port, in Pudong.

Shooting 135

The assailants then ordered the car to stop. It was already past 10 AM. They then forced Chen out of the car, and one of the assailants paid the driver Jin two yuan and four jiao. Jin then turned the car around and drove back the way he came. The assailants then held Chen Qinglu and walked forward for dozens of steps. The area was remote, and the assailants pulled out handguns and shot Chen. A total of six or seven shots were fired, with Chen being hit once in the chest, head, and right leg. He was injured in an instant, blood flowed profusely, and he fell to the ground in extreme pain. The assailants, seeing that their goal had been achieved, scattered and fled. Fortunately, patrol officer Zhang Lianglong of the Fourth Precinct of the Fifth District, accompanied by police chief He Shaoxiang, was patrolling and found Chen Qinglu lying in a pool of blood, barely breathing. They then helped him up and took him to the Sacred Heart Hospital at No. 41 Yangshupu Road for treatment.

Serious Injuries 136

On one hand, the bureau chief Jū Jìng was notified, and a large number of police officers were dispatched to search everywhere.

However, because of the time that had passed, the assailant was not caught. In the middle of the search, Inspector Zhāng and others, seeing that Chén had suffered severe injuries but was still conscious, asked for his name and occupation. Immediately, they used the telephone to notify the power company. Before long, they arrived at Sacred Heart Hospital, sending him into ward number 90. There, Doctor Hóu Yúnqīng of the hospital diagnosed him. He discovered that Chén had been shot once in the left chest, which was the most serious wound. The bullet entered through the back, pierced through the lung, and exited from the front chest. Another bullet had hit the right leg, entering straight from the buttock, but had not yet exited. The head had only been grazed slightly by a bullet. He immediately performed surgery, managing to extract the bullet from his leg. However, the injuries were still severe, and his life was in danger. Around 2 PM, Chén's family learned of what had happened. His older brother, Qìngfú, rushed to the hospital to visit him. Because Chén was in an ordinary ward, he negotiated with Sacred Heart Hospital to move him to a first-class ward. At the same time, he planned to have Doctor Niú Huìlín treat him. The Yángshùpǔ police station, having received a report from the power company, also dispatched detectives to Sacred Heart Hospital to investigate and inquire about the assailant's clothing and appearance from Chén in order to pursue him. The Municipal Public Security Bureau had also ordered all the detectives to investigate everywhere, so this case will not be difficult to solve.

Page 14

YMCA Held the Greater Shanghai Construction Movement Yesterday 137

Acting Mayor Yú Hóngjūn Speaks on the Greater Shanghai Plan

The Shanghai YMCA held the opening day of the Greater Shanghai Construction Movement yesterday. In the reading room of the YMCA, models and charts of various construction plans for the city center were displayed. From 10 AM to 9 PM, visitors came in an endless stream and it was extremely crowded. At 5:30 PM, there was a opening ceremony, and Mayor Wú was invited to give a speech. However, because Mayor Wú had just returned from Nánjīng and Shànghǎi and had other important matters, Secretary-General Yú Hóngjūn was delegated to attend and give a speech titled "(The Greater Shanghai Plan)." There was no ceremony at the opening. After the chairman introduced him, Yú immediately began his speech, saying, "Today, the YMCA is holding the Greater Shanghai Construction Movement. Mayor Wú originally intended to come in person to report to everyone, but because the mayor has just returned to Shànghǎi from Nánjīng and also has temporary urgent matters to deal with, he was unable to come in person, so I, as a brother, am representing him. Although Mayor Wú did not come in person, his spirit of construction is completely in line with everyone. Now, with the national crisis at hand, everyone in the country agrees that only construction can strengthen the country and save the nation. Therefore, the greatness of the spirit and the far-sightedness of the vision of the Greater Shanghai Construction Movement is enough to make us admire it. At the same time, I also feel that there are many enlightened people among the general public, but there are also quite a few who are living in a dream, indulging in ease and comfort. At this time, when everyone's work is completed, originally it should be a time for rest and entertainment, but they are willing to spend their precious time here to listen to the mayor's speech, which shows that they are extremely concerned about the construction of this city. If this kind of spirit can be displayed by the people of the whole country, then the future of China will certainly be very promising. As for the five characters of 'Greater Shanghai Construction,' those who do not know or are old in Shànghǎi will think that Shànghǎi has Shànghǎi City and Shànghǎi County, and at the same time, there are also the Public Concession and the French Concession, two special districts. Those who travel from Cáo Jiādù to the Concession and the city center must say they are going to Shànghǎi, and those who cross the Pǔjiāng River from the Concession to the city area must say they are going to Pǔdōng. But in fact, the area covered by the two characters 'Shànghǎi' is extremely broad and definitely not as narrow as that. Therefore, the meaning and future of Greater Shànghǎi contain unlimited hope. Everyone should observe that along the river in the existing concession area, most of the wharves belong to foreigners, and as a result, China's shipping industry has no way to develop. But foreigners also feel that within the concession, the land is small and the population is large, and there is no way to further develop. Therefore, they have taken the action of building roads beyond the boundary to seek expansion. However, why does the Greater Shànghǎi Plan not start with the existing urban areas of Zháběi and Nánshì, but instead looks for a new city center in the current city center area? Because it is easier to reorganize the old city center area, but it is very difficult to carry out a thorough reform. Therefore, in order to avoid being restricted by the environment, a new city center area is established near Jiāngwān to be the center of the entire city. This place is east of Pǔdōng, south of the concession, north of Wúsōng, and west of Zhēnrú. It has a deep-water port by the river where wharves can be built, and light railways can be built to connect water and land transportation. Commerce is extremely convenient. Usually, public buses travel to and from the city area in only twenty minutes, which is not much different from the time it takes to travel to and from the current municipal government. The cost of housing is low, and the air is fresh, making it very suitable for people to live in. Therefore, the municipal government is also greatly concerned about the housing problem for citizens. The municipal government has always not regarded publicity as its work, but regards work as publicity and actively carries it out. Although it has been hit by the January 28th Incident, it still tries its best to carry on. Now, the main roads have gradually been completed, and the new buildings of the municipal government were completed during the recent Mid-Autumn Festival. However, some people doubt why the municipal government's buildings are so magnificent, but in fact, it only seeks to be solid. Although the appearance is designed to impress future prosperity and development, the cost is not very high. On the other hand, in order to make the citizens believe, it must be done in this way to let the citizens know that the municipal government is truly sincere and not perfunctory, and to jointly assist the government in carrying out the project, for the sake of a permanent solution. Now, the water and electricity have been completely equipped. The second step of the plan is scheduled to be officially moved in on January 1st of next year, which will further strengthen the citizens' trust, so that the people will unite and build residential areas. The third step of the plan is to build the Yángzikǒu Commercial Port, build the Pǔjiāng Railway Bridge to connect Pǔdōng transportation, etc., all of which are the most important things in the plan. In short, foreigners have said that the prosperity of Rome cannot be achieved in one day. Therefore, the Greater Shanghai Plan cannot be achieved by a few colleagues in the municipal government alone. It requires everyone to work together, think for the public, and not make empty promises, and then nothing will be impossible."

Wusong Merchant Marine College Welcomes Sà Dǐngmíng 139

The Wusong Merchant Marine College of the Ministry of Communications was founded in the late Qing Dynasty. At that time, the person who managed and planned it to completion was Admiral Sà Dǐngmíng, a veteran of the navy. Sà also presided over the school administration for many years, so today many of the teachers of the school are his former students. In the middle of several changes, it was suspended. In 1929, as a result of the efforts of former President Yáng Zhì , it was restored. After the January 28th Incident, most of the school buildings were destroyed. Now, President Xú Jìjié is working hard to restore it, and the school buildings have been rebuilt. In the past two years, the school affairs have been showing a trend of increasing strictness and improvement. Now, the teachers and students of the school took the opportunity of Sà's coming to Shànghǎi for disaster relief for the people of Mǐn Province, and held a general assembly yesterday morning (the 20th) to welcome him, and invited Sà to give a speech, the general idea of which was to work hard to cultivate dangerous spirit, and create useful talents for the country. It was extremely prosperous. Then, former President Yáng gave a speech, especially paying attention to the item of physical education. Finally, President Xú gave a thank you speech, and then the whole group took a photo. It was not until the afternoon that they dispersed happily.

The Municipal Government Allocates Additional 30,000 Yuan for Dike Repair 146

The dikes in the Gāoqiáo and Wúsōng areas of this city were in danger at the beginning of last month due to the passage of a hurricane. The municipal government allocated 50,000 yuan to the Municipal Bureau of Public Works to hire workers to repair them. However, in the middle of last month, a second hurricane passed through, and the wind was even stronger than before, and the high tide was also at its peak, which caused even more damage to the east and west dikes. The Municipal Bureau of Public Works continued to rush to repair them on the one hand, and on the other hand, submitted another request to the municipal government for additional funding to facilitate the progress. The municipal government considered the importance of the dikes, and allocated another 30,000 yuan, ordering the Municipal Bureau of Public Works to quickly repair the destroyed dikes to avoid future troubles.

Discussion Items 150

After the report was completed, the discussion continued: (1) The repairs must be carried out during the small flood period. If it passes from the 24th of this month to the end of the month (that is, the sixth to twelfth day of the ninth lunar month), if the flood control project is not completed, it will be too late to plant wheat and broad beans. The reports from the counties are different, but the sandbars isolated in the sea are more urgent than the coastal areas of the mainland. If we wait for the completion of the review before discussing the construction, it will inevitably delay the planting of the small ripe crops. Should we make some changes and allocate at least the necessary funds to each county and inform them by telegram, limiting them to start work immediately within the small flood period next week, while at the same time having the engineering inspectors go to investigate the case separately? (Resolution) The association will allocate loans to the five counties, which will be properly handled by the local gentry of the five counties to rush to repair the dike breaches. The five counties will be supervised by their respective county governments. The allocation is estimated to be 15,000 yuan for Chuānshā, 7,000 yuan for Nánhuì, 18,000 yuan for Chóngmíng, 12,000 yuan for Bǎoshān, and 20,000 yuan for Qǐdōng. (2) The Nánhuì County Chief requested by telegram to issue seed grain, but there was no number. The Chuānshā County Chief informed by letter that the Hall of Consultations was separately verifying the seeds and would report by the end of the month. He also said that it is advisable to take this opportunity to select and distribute good seeds, which can improve agricultural production. Also, the Bǎoshān office reported that the sand-producing rice of each sand bank said that in addition to obtaining relief rice, the tenants will have three to four tenths of the rice this year. As long as the dikes can be repaired and the small ripe crops can be planted, there will be no problem next year. As for cotton and cotton seeds, it is a matter for next spring. Should we issue small ripe seeds now, or wait for the counties to report the exact number and type before reviewing and approving the case? (Resolution) After the counties report the exact number and type, we will review and approve the allocation. (3) The Nánhuì County Acting Chief requested by telegram to allocate 10,000 sets of cotton clothes and trousers, and the Chuānshā County requested by letter to issue 7,000 sets of cotton clothes and trousers. Please make a public decision on the case. (Resolution) After Chóng and Qǐ counties report, they will be reviewed and issued. (4) The Chóngmíng County Party Committee Executive Committee sent a letter requesting to release winter relief. How should it be handled? Please make a public decision on the case. (Resolution) Temporarily postpone the discussion. The rest of the discussion was completed, and the meeting was adjourned.

Southern Goods Industry Workers Demand Maintaining Original Conditions 151

General Assembly Held Yesterday to Discuss Response, First Negotiate with Capitalists

Dàgōngshè reports that the Shànghǎi Southern Goods Industry Workers' Union has recently received reports from members in various districts that capitalists are arbitrarily destroying the originally agreed-upon labor-capital conditions, resulting in a failure to maintain livelihoods, and requesting negotiations. After receiving the report, the union convened a joint meeting of the group leaders, directors, and supervisors of each district in the city at 1 PM yesterday, with more than 50 representatives attending. Chairman Yú Yàqiú reported the request letters and condition contents of each member. The following cases were immediately discussed: (1) It was decided to appoint six representatives to negotiate directly with the capitalists at 2 PM tomorrow, and Huáng Běnlì, Jīn Dōngtíng, Yáng Shìdé, Yú Yàqiú and other six people were appointed. (2) If there is still no result, how should we respond? (Resolution): (A) Report to the Party for assistance. (B) Convene a general assembly of city representatives next Sunday afternoon at 2 PM to discuss the response. (C) If necessary, organize a special committee. (3) How should we handle the unresolved cases of employees being laid off during the Lunar Mid-Autumn Festival? (Resolution) Submit to the higher-level mediation. (4) The manager of Déchāng in Bāxiānqiáo beat member Lǐ Gōng. It was resolved to submit to the party and government organs and hire lawyer Zhāng Juānshēng to file a lawsuit according to law. (5) The deadline for soliciting members. (Resolution) Submit to the representative assembly for discussion. The meeting was adjourned after the discussion.

Only Twenty Years Old, Yet Three Husbands - Zhāng Xiǎomèi Commits Bigamy, The Young Woman's Willful Love, Repeatedly Abandoned and Sold, The Original Husband Discovers The Truth and Asks the Court to Punish Her - The Result of the Trial is Five Months Imprisonment as a Warning 152

Zhāng Xiǎomèi, a woman from Yíxīng, is 21 years old and slightly attractive. When she was 18, in the autumn, she married Bì Fèngshēng, a plasterer from Chángzhōu. They lived in Zhōujiāqiáo Village, Yángshùpǔ, and the affection between the couple was harmonious. However, because the family gradually became poor, Bì became ill in January of this year, making it even more difficult to make a living. He quarreled with his wife every day. Xiǎomèi angrily went out to a broker near the Great World and was introduced to work as a helper at Wang's mansion, No. 19 Jiājí Road, French Concession. She sent a letter to her husband. Because Bì was unable to support her, he had to let her do as she pleased. Unexpectedly, Zhāng Xiǎomèi recently became acquainted with Jīn Liùgēn, a rogue from the same village, and rented a small house on Běihǎi Road. They were as loving as a couple, living together day and night. Later, because their income could not meet their expenses, and all their money was gone, there was no way to support themselves. Then there was Gù Quángēn, a man from Wúxī, who was 23 years old and still unmarried. He lived in a bungalow on Dàliánwān Road and worked as a tinsmith. He was very honest. Jīn Liùgēn knew about him and asked two friends, Shěn Bǐnghuá and Wú Shàoxiān, to act as matchmakers. He falsely changed Zhāng Xiǎomèi's surname to Jīn, posing as his younger sister, and married her to Gù Quángēn for a betrothal gift of 140 yuan. They got married at the nearby Tàihé Restaurant on the 17th of this month. The day before, the original husband, Bì Fèngshēng, discovered the truth and asked Shěn Bǐnghuá, who was acting as the matchmaker. A big conflict broke out. Shěn's wife, Zhū, secretly reported to the Yúlín Road Police Station, who sent Detective Wū Wéndá to investigate clearly. He immediately brought the woman, Jīn Xiǎomèi, to the police station and sent her to the women's prison for temporary detention. Yesterday morning, she was escorted to the Criminal Court No. 3 of the First Special District Court. Attorney Zhāng Tiānyīn of the police station explained the situation in detail and said that the offender Jīn Liùgēn was at large and could not be arrested, and Gù Quángēn married the defendant as his wife, and there was a marriage certificate, which was presided over by Jīn Liùgēn. He submitted the certificate for inspection, saying that the police station accused the defendant of bigamy according to Article 254 of the Criminal Law and filed a public prosecution, and that Jīn Liùgēn and the defendant had colluded to commit the crime, requesting strict punishment. Then, Bì Fèngshēng and Gù Quángēn stated the process. Wú Shàoxiān, Gù's matchmaker, said that the betrothal gift was handed over to Jīn Liùgēn, and he did not know that there were such entanglements. When questioned, the defendant confessed that she was fooled by Jīn Liùgēn, saying that she would pay the money to her original husband, Bì Fèngshēng, to break off the relationship. The rest of the confession was vague. Judge Liú Yùguì sentenced Jīn Xiǎomèi, that is, Zhāng Xiǎomèi, to five months imprisonment as a warning.

Judgment in the Counterfeit Certificate Case; Sichuan Zhonghe Bank Discovers Counterfeit Certificates; Intricate Investigation of Wansuo's Cigarette Contract 153

Lu Fengzhu Sentenced to Two Years Imprisonment, Will Appeal

Lu Fengzhu, former Executive Committee Member of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce and current committee member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and General Manager of the Zhonghua Printing House, was recently sentenced to two years imprisonment by the Criminal Division of the First Special District Court for counterfeiting documents. The details of this case are unusually complex and significant, involving litigation that has lasted for several years. The reporter, after several days of investigation, has recorded the findings below. The case originates from the Zhonghe Bank in Chongqing, Sichuan, which was established by Liu Xiang and other military and business figures. In the 15th year of the Republic (1926), to facilitate financial circulation in the market, the bank's board of directors resolved to issue (non-interest-bearing certificates), with a face value of 3 million yuan. Due to the lack of sophisticated printing facilities in Sichuan, Sun Shubei, the bank's general manager, entrusted Tang Bingzhang, then of the Shanghai Yuchang Match Factory, to contact the Commercial Press for printing the certificates. Wang Hongbin, the factory director of Yuchang Factory, knew Xi Yanggao, the manager of the Great China Printing Bureau. Wang introduced Tang, and after satisfactory negotiations, the Great China Printing Bureau was commissioned to undertake the printing. It was specified that 800,000 certificates would be printed, with 200,000 being 10-yuan certificates, 100,000 being 5-yuan certificates, and 500,000 being 1-yuan certificates. Later, the bank instructed that the number of 1-yuan certificates be reduced by 50,000 and the number of 5-yuan certificates be increased by 50,000, increasing the face value to 3.2 million yuan. A contract was signed, specifying that the printing plates used would be intaglio, the paper would be American banknote paper, the printing fee would be 31,200 yuan, and the original plates would be destroyed after printing. However, the Zhonghe side, deeply concerned about potential fraud such as underreporting the quantity and the appearance of counterfeit certificates with the same plates and paper, required the Great China Printing Bureau to provide a guarantee. Xi Yanggao then enlisted Lu Fengzhu to act as a guarantor, stipulating that if any of the above events occurred in the future, the Great China Printing Bureau and Lu Fengzhu would be liable for compensating all losses. If it was found that the fraud was committed by someone within the printing bureau, they would be sent to court for prosecution and no leniency would be shown. Therefore, the signatories on the contract were Tang Bingzhang, representing Zhonghe, Xi Yanggao, representing Great China, Lu Fengzhu of the Zhonghua Printing House as the guarantor, Liu Yingcai and Wang Hongbin as witnesses, and Xi Yuquan as the contract drafter. These certificates were fully paid off from the time they were printed until the 20th year of the Republic (1931), and were issued by Zhonghe Bank. Not long after they circulated in the market, a large number of counterfeit certificates with the same serial numbers were discovered. Consequently, in the 21st year of the Republic (1932), Zhonghe, with the approval of the 21st Army Headquarters and the Chongqing Municipal Government, recalled the certificates. Unexpectedly, Liao Yinxiian, a section chief of the Army Headquarters, ordered someone to present 1,000 yuan worth of Zhonghe 10-yuan certificates for redemption. After examination by the bank, they were found to be counterfeit. When questioned about their origin, they claimed to have obtained them from a Chen's jade shop on Mihua Street. An investigation was conducted at the jade shop, which revealed that they had been obtained from Wang Hongbin's home at No. 64 Yangliu Street. Sun Shubei, the general manager of Zhonghe, immediately reported this to the Public Security Bureau. The bureau chief, She Zili, led police officers, accompanied by local gentry and officials, to Wang's home for a search. Wang and his wife, Shuzhen, were found collecting luggage, preparing to flee. They were immediately arrested, and 57,140 yuan worth of counterfeit certificates and a small leather suitcase were found. Wang Hongbin was found in the suitcase.

Criminal Sentence for Leaked Exam Questions 154

During the Shanghai Municipal Middle School Entrance Examination, it was discovered that student Xie Ying had pre-copied exam questions. After investigation, it was found that when the Bureau of Education entrusted the Nanjing Printing Company to print the exam questions, the company owner, Zhang Jieliang, had given the questions to Xie Ying's brother, Xie Zhen. They were both immediately taken into custody and prosecuted by the District Court. After the debate concluded, Judge Qian announced the verdict yesterday: Zhang Jieliang was sentenced to six months imprisonment for misappropriating items held in his professional capacity; Xie Zhen was sentenced to four months imprisonment for inciting misappropriation; and Xie Ying was sentenced to two months imprisonment for receiving stolen goods, with each sentence suspended for one year.

Bao Rongtang and Son, Owners of Longxing Gold Shop, Sued; Mrs. Yang Accuses Father-in-Law of Cutting Off Expenses; Demands 30,000 Yuan for Support and Division of Inheritance 155

Second Hearing Yesterday, Defendants Still Failed to Appear, Postponement Again

Bao Jianfu, owner of Longxing Gold Shop on Edward Road, is the eldest grandson of Bao Aofeng, the founder of Yingfeng Qianzhuang, a financial institution in Xian Gua Street in the city, which has been established for nearly 70 years and is considered a pioneer in the financial world in Shanghai. Aofeng had two sons, the elder named Rongtang and the younger Wenwei. Rongtang also had two sons, the elder being Jianfu and the younger Qiankui. Wenwei, however, had no offspring, so Qiankui was adopted as his heir. However, Qiankui suddenly passed away in the 6th year of the Republic (1917) shortly after marrying Mrs. Yang, following his grandfather and father (adoptive father). Therefore, Aofeng's entire estate of six or seven hundred thousand yuan was controlled by Rongtang and Jianfu. Rongtang is now old and resides in a self-purchased Western-style house at No. 72 Chunpingfang, Hedde Road in West Shanghai, enjoying a comfortable and prestigious life, spending his remaining years in leisure. He has entrusted all household affairs to his son, Jianfu, who has been able to arbitrarily dispose of the family property. Longxing Gold Shop is ostensibly opened by Jianfu with his own funds, but the capital is actually misappropriated from the property jointly owned with Mrs. Yang. It is only because he deceives Mrs. Yang, a woman, that he dares to do whatever he wants. Not long after her husband's death, she gave birth to a posthumous daughter, who unfortunately died young. She then raised a son, determined to remain chaste and raise her son so that he could inherit the property that her late husband should have received. For more than ten years, despite being discriminated against by her father-in-law and brother-in-law, she has only been given meager living expenses, barely enough for congee. She has endured hardships and swallowed her voice in silence, spending her days in monotony and misery, refraining from arguing with them. Unexpectedly, Rongtang and his son have taken advantage of the widow's weakness and suddenly cut off the meager living expenses they had been providing on April 1st of this year, leaving Mrs. Yang destitute. Faced with this oppression, she has no choice but to resort to the law in the hope of preserving her life. She has retained lawyer Hu Jue to represent her in filing a lawsuit with the First Special District Court, accusing her father-in-law Bao Rongtang and brother-in-law Bao Jianfu of failing to provide support and of privately selling off the inheritance, requesting the court to order a division of the property and payment of 30,000 yuan in support. She argues that the defendants disregard the feelings for her late husband and are not only unpitying but also unusually harsh. The property that the plaintiff should have inherited under the name of her late husband's uncle, Wenwei, has also been entirely misappropriated by the defendants and secretly sold off, yielding tens of thousands of yuan. Even based on joint property rights, it is invalid under the law without obtaining the plaintiff's consent and signature. The defendants have seized this ancestral property for themselves and indulged in luxurious living with beautiful wives and concubines, while oppressing and threatening others, bullying widows and orphans. In addition to Wenwei's property, there is also jointly inheritable property, which she fears may be continuously sold off secretly. She requests the court to order the defendants to hand over all of the property, distribute it fairly, and pay a lump sum of 30,000 yuan for support. The case has already been heard once, but the defendants failed to appear, so it was postponed until yesterday for another hearing. However, the defendants, Bao Rongtang and his son, still failed to appear, making it impossible to begin the hearing. Judge Qiao then ordered that the case be rescheduled and the defendants be summoned to court again for questioning.

And the joint guarantee contract of Wu Fu Company signed by his younger brother Zhi’an, Xi Youtao (namely Xi Yuquan), Lu Fengzhu, Chen Yiting, etc. The content of the contract is to sell the Golden Beauty Ju Xin brand cigarettes. After Wang was arrested, he confessed in front of Tang Dizhi, the director of the finance department of the army headquarters, She Zili, the director of the Public Security Bureau, Zeng Ziwei, the division commander, and Wen Shaohe, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, that he, Lu Fengzhu, Xi Yanggao, Xi Youtao, and Chen Yiting had overprinted and used the original Zhonghe certificates and were willing to use the property to compensate. An investigation revealed that the contract for selling cigarettes by the Wufu Company contained many questionable words, such as "border flowers (new and old colors)" and "(overprinting)", which are not necessary for cigarettes, and that a profit of more than 50,000 was made in a short period of time, which is impossible for sales. Therefore, it is believed that this contract is a code for Wang and Xi to counterfeit and use certificates, with Golden cigarettes actually meaning full gold, Beauty having five United States, which is determined to represent the 10-yuan and 5-yuan certificates, and Juxin not existing as a brand, but must represent the 1-yuan certificates. Wang was sent to the military headquarters for brutal interrogation, and Wang was shot last year. Meanwhile, Zhonghe Bank sent representative Zeng Binghui to Shanghai, hired lawyer Tan Yigong, and sued Xi Yuquan (because Xi Yanggao had died), Lu Fengzhu, Wang Zhi’an, Chen Yiting, etc. to the First Special District Court in the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931) for forging documents and other crimes, and demanded compensation for losses of 300,000 yuan (because Zhonghe discovered counterfeit certificates (amounting to more than 370,000 yuan)). After investigation and evidence review by the Special First Court, the case was only concluded this month. Only the defendant Lu Fengzhu appeared in court, and the rest failed to be summoned. Yesterday, Judge Xue Lanru announced the judgment, the main text of which was: Lu Fengzhu was sentenced to two years imprisonment, and the trials of Xi Yuquan, Wang Zhi'an, and Chen Yiting were suspended. The attached lawsuit was transferred to the civil court for trial. During the appeal period, Lu Fengzhu was allowed to post a bail of 3,000 yuan. It is said that Lu was dissatisfied with the judgment and will appeal.

Liu Chuanxian Rape Case of Chen Jinxian Continued Trial Yesterday 156

Liu Chuanxian, a Yangzhou native, 26 years old, a barber at the Da Zhonghua Barber Shop at No. 122 Dongxinqiao Street, French Concession, on the 27th of last month at 12:00 pm, took advantage of the fact that the Ningbo woman Chen Zhao and her husband who lived in the attic upstairs had gone out to see a play. He sneaked into the room and forcibly raped Chen Jinxian (14 years old), the younger sister of the Chen woman who was already asleep. Afterwards, he prevented the girl from crying out. The Zhang girl endured in silence and washed away the blood stains on her underwear and bedding. Later, because her lower body was injured and in pain, she told her aunt, who told the girl's elder brother and sister-in-law, who then reported to the detective Liu Achang, who was dispatched by the police, and Liu was arrested. The girl was sent to the hospital for an examination, which confirmed that she had been raped. Liu was sent to the Second Special District Court and prosecuted for the crime of obstructing public morals. All the details have been reported in various newspapers. After the court hearing, it was ordered that the victim submit the blood-stained clothing, trousers, and bedding to the court for verification. Yesterday, Judge Zhang Zhaoyou continued the trial in the Criminal Court One. According to the defendant's confession, the complainant pointed out that the time of the rape was when he was playing with friends at the Great World, but the Zhu witness he named could not be found by the court. The complainant, Chen Zhao, along with her younger sister Chen Jinxian, brought the clothing, trousers, and bedding to court, stating that the blood stains on the clothing had been washed away and could not be identified. The official ordered that the clothing be retained by the court for medical examination and that the hearing be postponed to 9:00 am on the 30th after a defense lawyer was appointed. The defendant was remanded in custody pending further instructions.

Gu Xiaomei, a young girl from Songjiang, 19 years old, with a beautiful appearance, came to Shanghai in June of the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931). Through the introduction of Lu Gen, a Danyang native who sells eyeglasses, she met Cai Xiaoyun, a Changzhou native who makes photo frames (34 years old). Seeing the girl's beautiful face, he became lustful and used sweet words and all kinds of temptations. Xiaomei, being young and inexperienced, was seduced. At first, they only met secretly in a concession hotel, and then he tricked her into living with him in his photo frame shop at No. 31 Yongheli, Kangti Road, French Concession. Cai employed more than ten workers and had two younger brothers, one named Xiaozhong (39 years old) and the other Xiaobing (23 years old), who both assisted in the shop. However, the three Cai brothers were inherently violent, and Cai's attitude towards Xiaomei had long changed. After she gave birth to a boy in August of last year, who died of illness on August 12th of this year, according to the lunar calendar, he began to abuse her from time to time. He punched and kicked Xiaomei and, with Xiaobing's assistance, inflicted humiliation and slapped her several times, beating her all over. He tore off her lined jacket, pushed her down the stairs, and drove her out. Xiaomei only wore a single short shirt and trousers when she left the house. Having no relatives or friends in Shanghai, she spent the night on the road and contemplated suicide. Yesterday morning, while passing the old Jiaochang in the city inside Laobei Men, she intended to commit suicide by jumping into the Huangpu River at the Bund. She was spotted by a patrol police officer from Dadongmen Post of the Third Section of the First District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who took her to the station. Moreover, the ceremonial guards sent by various organizations, charities, and fellow villagers' associations from Huzhou and other places, as well as various commercial, academic, and labor circles, were extremely distinctive and rarely seen in Shanghai. It was not appropriate to reject their kindness. However, on the 22nd (tomorrow), the funeral procession would be grand, and there would be many workers. All Workers of the Fulun Shuanggong Silk Factory Resumed Work Yesterday Morning 164

More than 400 workers of the Fulun Hengshuang Gong Silk Factory at the end of Tianbao Road, Hongkou, went on strike for no reason after the afternoon of the 6th. After mediation by the Social Bureau on the 16th, it was decided that all workers would resume work on the 18th. However, only 200 workers went to work on that day, and the remaining half still refused to resume work. On the same afternoon, they went on strike again. The capital side believed that the losses from the resumption of work and the strike were extremely heavy, so they notified the labor union to ask all workers to go to the factory to collect their unpaid wages. The factory sounded the whistle and issued the accumulated wages the day before, and all the workers all attended to resume work. Yesterday morning, the factory started, and all the workers went to the factory to work, earlier than usual. The strike dispute was resolved.

Qibao Public Groups Urge Dredging of Section Six of Puhui Pond; Municipal Public Works Bureau Decides to Start Work Soon 165

Since the Songhu War Zone Rehabilitation Association of the National Government allocated funds for dredging, all sections of the Puhui Pond River in West Shanghai have been completed and the dams have been opened. Small ferries come and go, and traffic in the towns along the pond has become convenient. However, the section from the Paifangwan to Tianyaoqiao dam (ie, section six) has not been dredged yet. All ferries often run aground in this section, so they can only open to Zhongshan Road and transport passengers by car. Recently, Shen Yingpeng, Gu Junjie, Li Youxian, Shen Cai Geng, Li Qixian, etc., the leaders of various public groups such as the Qishen Town Party Department, District Office, Chamber of Commerce, and various industry associations, jointly presented a ring to Song Ziwen, chairman of the National Government Songhu War Zone Rehabilitation Association, requesting that he order the Municipal Public Works Bureau to expedite the dredging in order to comfort the people's hopes and achieve complete success. It is now learned that the Municipal Public Works Bureau has been ordered to prepare for dredging and will soon cut the dam and start work.

Wu Song Road Obstacle Buildings Removed, Road Line Neat 166

All temporary houses in the Wu Song area post-war reconstruction project that occupied the road surface without permits had previously been notified by the Shanghai Municipal Public Works Bureau to remove them when the road surface was being built. Afterwards, because each household had suffered disasters and had not recovered, they requested an extension from the Wu Song Chamber of Commerce and the Municipal Office, and disputes arose. This was reported in the previous newspaper. Subsequently, Municipal Committee Tang Chengzong reported the situation to the Public Works Bureau, asking for consideration of the merchants' difficulties and granting an extension, and requesting that demolition fees be issued to each demolition household. The Public Works Bureau approved the extension until the end of September. Those who removed the buildings by the deadline were given a demolition fee of two yuan per square meter of occupied land for a flat roof and four yuan per square meter for a multi-story building. An investigation found that a total of 53 households should be demolished, and they have been demolished or taken in order. Therefore, the route is more orderly than before. However, eight households, including Zhengtong, Gongxiangtai, and Wanlong, are still taking a wait-and-see attitude. The Public Works Bureau has ordered the Wu Song Municipal Office to notify each household that if the deadline is exceeded, the demolition fees will be cancelled and they will be ordered to remove the buildings to complete the restoration project.

Verdict on Wang Zhihao's Case of Selling Red Pills 168

Lu Zhulin, an investigator from the French police station, and Liu Jinrong, a prostitute, patrolled to the intersection of Min Guo Road and Maidi'an Road at 11:00 PM on the 5th of this month, and arrested Wang Zhihao from Shaoxing, who was carrying red pills privately. He was carrying six bags of red pills, totaling 6,000 pills. According to his confession, Xia Jisheng, also known as Xiao Shaoxing, the owner of the red pill shop at No. 9 Ailaige Road, entrusted him to take them somewhere to sell. When the investigators took Wang to Xia's house to search, Xia heard the sound and escaped from the roof. Only two employees, Fan Jin and Yuan Shunzi, were caught. Raw materials for red pills and pill-making equipment were seized and taken to the police station and sent to the Second Special Court for prosecution. The details of the interrogation have been recorded in previous reports. The interrogation has now concluded. Yesterday, Judge Zhang sentenced Fan Jin and Yuan Shunzi to six months of imprisonment each in the Criminal Court No. 1, with a fine of 500 yuan. Wang Zhihao was sentenced to three months of imprisonment with a fine of 300 yuan. If the fines are converted into imprisonment, each three yuan will be counted as one day. The number of days of detention before the judgment is confirmed will be used to offset one day of imprisonment for every two days. The red pill drug materials and equipment will be confiscated and burned.

Guo Changxi's Case Scheduled for Sentencing 169

Guo Changxi, a 26-year-old man from Yangzhou, residing at No. 97, Xinkang Lane, Kangnao Road, previously worked at the Weida Hotel opened by Chen Weida at No. 593 Xiafei Road in the French Concession, serving as a receptionist and mailman. Last month, he had a gambling dispute with his colleagues late at night, which was discovered by the French manager and reported to the hotel owner. When paying wages at the end of the month, the hotel owner wanted to deduct five jiao of wages, which Guo refused. After Guo quit, he threatened Fei Enqing, a worker who was hired later. Soon, the hotel owner also received an anonymous insulting and threatening letter, suspecting that Guo was the perpetrator, but there was no evidence to prove it. On the 9th of this month, when Guo went to the Weida Hotel to ask for a deposit slip, Chen Weida asked Guo to provide a receipt. Later, it was discovered that the "Da" character on the receipt matched the handwriting of the "Da" character on the threatening letter. Therefore, he reported it to the French police station, which sent an investigator to detain Guo on the 11th of this month and send him to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and investigation. Yesterday, Judge Zhang Chaozuo continued the trial in the Criminal Court No. 1. First, the police station's lawyer stated that the police station had investigated and the defendant denied writing the threatening letter, and no evidence was found, so the court should verify the matter. He also presented the letter as evidence. Then, the plaintiff, Chen Weida, stated that the defendant was fined for gambling and refused to quit, and often came to threaten and harass him. Later, he received a threatening letter and reported the situation to the police to arrest the defendant. When the defendant Guo Changxi was interrogated, he flatly denied writing the letter and threatening anyone. He said that he went to ask for the deposit slip on the 9th of this month and was not allowed to have it, so a dispute arose, and the hotel owner reported the case to the police and arrested him. After the court verified the confession, it announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for the 25th. The defendant was ordered to provide a reliable hotel guarantor who could be summoned at any time to await instructions.

Development of the Chinese Pathological Laboratory 170

Mr. Wang Yongsan has long studied medicine and is particularly proficient in chemical testing. He served as a chemical tester at Peking Union Medical College Hospital for many years. After coming to Shanghai, he served as the director of various pathological laboratories. As time passed, his experience became richer. He has now established the Chinese Pathological Laboratory on the third floor of No. 267 Jiangxi Road. Since its opening, many patients and doctors have entrusted him with chemical testing. Mr. Wang, based on his experience, performs chemical tests and examinations with great accuracy, and his service spirit is also extremely diligent.
